1001 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Beeman v. Department of Health & Mental Hygiene


No. 1353, SEPTEMBER TERM, 1994


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


105 Md. App. 147; 658 A.2d 1172; 1995 Md. App. LEXIS 102



June 2, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: The Name of this Case has been Corrected by the Court June 20, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Allegany County. J. Frederick Sharer, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] APPEAL DISMISSED. COSTS TO BE PAID ONE-HALF BY APPELLANT AND ONE-HALF BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Allegany County (Maryland), which affirmed a decision authorizing appellee Department of Health and Mental Hygiene (agency) to administer a series of drugs without the patient's consent.


OVERVIEW: The patient was involuntarily committed to a mental health facility and refused to take certain drugs prescribed by her psychiatrist. A Clinical Review Panel (CRP) was convened and authorized the administration of a series of drugs at a wide range of doses. An Administrative Law Judge (ALJ) agreed with the decision and the circuit court affirmed. The court dismissed the appeal. The court noted that the issues presented in the appeal were moot because the ALJ's order had expired and the patient had been released. However, because the court found that the forced administration of medication was a matter of important public concern and an issue likely to recur and evade judicial review, the court considered the patient's substantive complaints. The court held that the CRP had the power to approve the forced administration of antidyskinetic drugs to treat the side effects of appropriate psychotropic medications. The court also held that the CRP had authority to approve a series of medications and a wide range of dosages, provided they were requested by a treating psychiatrist.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the patient's appeal of a judgment affirming a decision to authorize the agency to administer drugs to the patient without her consent.

 

1002 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Department of Health & Mental Hygiene v. Riverview Nursing Centre


No. 958, September Term, 1994


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


104 Md. App. 593; 657 A.2d 372; 1995 Md. App. LEXIS 86



April 27, 1995, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY REVERSED; CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTION THAT THE CIRCUIT COURT AFFIRM THE DECISION OF THE NURSING HOME APPEAL BOARD; APPELLEE TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Department of Health and Mental Hygiene (department), challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which reversed the decision of the Nursing Home Appeal Board (board). The board had affirmed the department's decision to disallow a portion of appellee nursing home's claimed Medicaid reimbursement for nursing home services.


OVERVIEW: The department issued a decision to disallow a portion of the nursing home's claimed Medicaid reimbursement for nursing home services. The board affirmed the department's decision, but the circuit court reversed the board's affirmance. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded with directions for the circuit court to affirm the board's decision. The court held that the circuit court failed to give appropriate weight to the department's long-standing and consistent application of the interest-offset rule. The court noted that the circuit court might have overlooked completely the department's consistent interpretative approach, as expressed in five prior cases. The court held that the department demonstrated that its interpretation was reasonable, consistent, and longstanding.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment and remanded with directions that the circuit court affirm the board's decision, which affirmed the department's decision to disallow a portion of the nursing home's Medicaid reimbursement claims.

 

1003 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Brooks v. State


No. 836, September Term, 1994


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


104 Md. App. 203; 655 A.2d 1311; 1995 Md. App. LEXIS 75



March 30, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore County. John F. Fader, II, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which convicted defendant of first degree felony murder and robbery with a dangerous and deadly weapon. After defendant waived her right to jury sentencing, the trial court, sitting without a jury, imposed a sentence of life without parole.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of first degree felony murder and robbery with a dangerous and deadly weapon, defendant waived her right to jury sentencing. The trial court imposed a sentence of life without parole and defendant appealed. Defendant argued that the trial judge erred by refusing to instruct the jury that all murder was presumed to be murder in the second degree. Defendant also argued that consideration of the underlying felony of robbery in both the guilt/innocence and sentencing phases of the trial violated her right to be free from cruel and unusual punishment. The court disagreed and affirmed the judgment, holding that the instructions were clear that the state was required to prove every element of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt and that the requested instruction would have added nothing. The court also held that because Maryland's capital sentencing scheme genuinely narrowed the class of felony murder defendants who were death-eligible, the use of the underlying felony as an aggravating factor did not offend U.S. Const. amend. VIII.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and the sentence imposed. The court held that the requested instruction regarding the presumption for second degree murder would have added nothing to the instructions regarding the state's burden of proof. The court also held that there was no evidence that the trial court's comments regarding the possible suspension of a life sentence had any effect on defendant's decision to waive jury sentencing.

 

1004 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Caretti v. Colonnade Ltd. Partnership


No. 1158, September Term, 1994


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


104 Md. App. 131; 655 A.2d 64; 1995 Md. App. LEXIS 60



March 7, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore City. Thomas Ward, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractor sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which denied appellant's motion for a mechanic's lien against residential condominium property sold at foreclosure sale.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contractor attempted to establish a mechanic's lien against part of a condominium project where he performed work. The trial court denied appellant's motion and appellant sought review. The court noted that there was a serious problem arising from the interplay between the Mechanic's Lien Law, Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. §§ 9-101--9-110, and the Uniform Arbitration Act because if the court were required to actually adjudicate disputes that were subject to arbitration, in order to determine whether a lien should be established, the arbitration agreement would be frustrated. On the other, if the court deferred consideration of an interlocutory order establishing a lien, appellant could be left unprotected for a considerable period of time. However, the court found it unnecessary to resolve the problem because the property that would have been subject to a mechanic's lien had been sold at a foreclosure sale and appellant had failed to join the unit owners as necessary parties. The court affirmed the trial court's denial of a lien.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant's attempt to establish a mechanic's lien against a condominium property because appellant had failed to join the individual unit owners as necessary parties.

 

1005 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Kohli v. LOOC


No. 765, September Term, 1994


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


103 Md. App. 694; 654 A.2d 922; 1995 Md. App. LEXIS 49; 66 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P43,497



March 2, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore County. J. William Hinkel, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTION TO VACATE THE DECISION AND ORDER OF THE HUMAN RELATIONS COMMISSION AND TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE APPEAL BOARD OF THE COMMISSION FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION.

COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which affirmed the decision rendered in favor of appellees, a pizza corporation and others, to dismiss appellant's complaint filed with the Maryland Commission on Human Relations, alleging religious discrimination arising out of the failure of appellees to hire him due to his refusal to shave the beard he wore for religious purposes.


OVERVIEW: The question for the court on appeal concerned not what standard of review the courts applied, but rather what was the standard of review that the final agency decision-maker applied in reviewing the intermediate administrative decision of the administrative law judge (ALJ). The determination of whether the pizza corporation would have suffered undue hardship by accommodating the applicant was a mixed question of law and fact, to which the more restricted standard of review applied, if that was what the agency rule required. The court found that it was evident that the commission, in reversing the ALJ, did not consider whether a reasoning mind could have reasonably reached the conclusions that it did. The commission never determined that the ALJ could not have adequately supported its conclusions based upon the evidence presented. Under these circumstances, where legal error was present in both the circuit court's and the commission's decisions, the appropriate remedy was to remand the case to the agency for a determination of whether the ALJ's decision was supported by substantial evidence. The court based this result upon its policy of according respect to the agency's findings.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed. The case was remanded to that court with directions to vacate the decision and order and further remand to the commission.

 

1006 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Icgoren v. State


No. 827, SEPTEMBER TERM, 1994


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


103 Md. App. 407; 653 A.2d 972; 1995 Md. App. LEXIS 32



February 10, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Howard County. Raymond J. Kane, Jr., JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Howard County (Maryland), which found him guilty of first degree murder, robbery with a dangerous and deadly weapon, robbery, common law assault, and common law battery. He was subsequently sentenced to a term of imprisonment for life.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued the charges against him should have been dismissed because he had been denied his right to a speedy trial. The court held that the 180 day rule, Md. R. Crim. Causes 4-271 did not apply to retrials. Since his prior trial had resulted in a hung jury, only the time between the second mistrial and appellant's third trial could be considered. Since this period was less than a year, it was presumptively of constitutional dimension. The court held it was required to balance the length of the delay and the reason for it against appellant's right to a speedy trial. Since the trial was held on the date it was set, with the agreement of defense counsel, appellant's rights were not violated. The fact of the first trial did not nullify the pretrial hearing on the motion to suppress appellant's statements. Under the rule of the case doctrine, the trial court did not err in adhering to the prior rulings. The court found no unconstitutional suppression of evidence where there was mere speculation as to the quality of "lost" evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence.

 

1007 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Department of Human Resources v. Thompson


No. 489, SEPTEMBER TERM, 1994


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


103 Md. App. 175; 652 A.2d 1183; 1995 Md. App. LEXIS 19



February 3, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore County. James T. Smith, Jr., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Child Care Administration (CCA) sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which reversed the judgment of the Office of Administration Hearings' (OAH) administrative law judge (ALJ) affirming the CCA's denial of appellee applicant's application for day care registration.


OVERVIEW: Applicant sought a day care license and listed her husband as a resident of her home. The department of social services (DSS) had previously determined that the applicant's husband had abused their daughter. The CCA denied her application for day care registration due to the past finding of abuse. On appeal to the OAH, the ALJ held a hearing but did not consider applicant's evidence that the abuse did not occur. The court found that in the absence of any legal determination of actual child abuse, and where the alleged abuser was not afforded any forum to challenge the DSS finding, the DSS determination of child abuse could not preclude the applicant from challenging the merits of the agency's abuse finding in a subsequent licensing proceeding. Because the DSS investigation did not result in a final determination of guilt, the agency's internal investigation could not have a preclusive effect in a subsequent proceeding. The court concluded that the applicant's procedural due process rights were violated by the denial of an opportunity to contest the accusation of abuse. The ALJ was required to consider evidence presented by the applicant, and her daughter's testimony was admissible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment reversing the decision that upheld the denial of the applicant's application for day care registration.

 

1008 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Cromwell v. Ward


No. 617, SEPTEMBER TERM, 1994


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


102 Md. App. 691; 651 A.2d 424; 1995 Md. App. LEXIS 9



January 4, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore County. Lawrence Daniels, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from the judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) affirming the order of the Zoning Board of Appeals granting a height variance for an accessory building already built by appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellee's act of constructing a building of such a height as to produce a roof pitched at the angle he desired caused the roof to extend above the fifteen-foot height limit. The Zoning Board of Appeals granted appellee a height variance. The circuit court affirmed the order. On appeal, the court found that a property's peculiar characteristic relating only and uniquely to that property must exist in conjunction with the ordinance's more severe impact on the specific property because of the property's uniqueness before any consideration will be given to whether practical difficulty or unnecessary hardship exists. The court reversed, holding that practical difficulty or unnecessary hardship for zoning variance purposes could not generally be self-inflicted; however, it was not the purpose of variance procedures to effect a legalization of a property owner's intentional or unintentional violations of zoning requirements. Where administrative entities such as the zoning authorities took it upon themselves to ignore the provisions of the statutes enacted by the legislative branch of government, they substituted their policies for those of the policy-makers.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the circuit court affirming the order of the Zoning Board of Appeals grant a height variance for an accessory building already built by appellee.

 

1009 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Curry v. Department of Pub. Safety & Correctional Servs.


Nos. 360, September Term, 1994, No. 553, September Term, 1994


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


102 Md. App. 620; 651 A.2d 390; 1994 Md. App. LEXIS 178



December 30, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 6, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: TWO APPEALS FROM THE Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (#360). Circuit Court for Washington County (#553). Eugene M. Lerner (#360), Daniel W. Moylan (#553), JUDGES.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] IN APPEAL NO. 360, JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT. IN APPEAL NO. 553, JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR WASHINGTON COUNTY REVERSED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state employee (employee) sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Ann Arundel County (Maryland) which affirmed a Secretary of Personnel decision to uphold his disciplinary suspension for drunk driving while off duty. Appellant Department of Corrections (department) challenged a decision by the Circuit Court of Washington County (Maryland) to reverse a similar suspension of appellee state employee (employee).


OVERVIEW: The employees brought separate actions in separate trial courts, challenging the validity of the department's internal disciplinary rule that allowed it to discipline employees convicted alcohol related offenses. The employees argued that Md. Ann. Code art. 27 § 641(c) prevented the department from disciplining them after pleading nolo contendere to drunk driving. One trial court affirmed the suspension and another reversed. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court that affirmed the suspension and reversed the trial court that reversed the suspension. The court held that § 641(c) did not protect against disciplinary suspension because suspension did not impose a legal disability on the employees. The court held that Exec. Order No. 01.01.1991.16 permitted the department to impose appropriate disciplinary actions for off the workplace alcohol offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that affirmed the suspension of the employee pursuant to internal disciplinary rules. The court reversed the trial court judgment that reversed the suspension of the employee pursuant to internal disciplinary rules.

 

1010 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


In re Adoption/Guardianship Nos. CAA92-10852 & CAA92-10853


No. 427, September Term, 1994


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


103 Md. App. 1; 651 A.2d 891; 1994 Md. App. LEXIS 167



December 5, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: First Correction December 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Prince George's County. David Gray Ross, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), terminated appellant father's parental rights of twin brothers and granted guardianship rights to appellee department of social services. The father appealed arguing that the court violated Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 5-313 (1989) when it terminated his parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The father claimed that the trial court improperly terminated his parental rights. The court agreed and reversed the judgment. First, there was not sufficient evidence presented by the department of social services to meet its burden of establishing by clear and convincing evidence that the father's parental rights should have been terminated and that the best interests of the children would have been served in the custody of foster parents rather than in his care or the custody of a member of his family, as required by Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 5-313 (1989). Second, the department of social services failed to provide the father with those services that it was statutorily obligated to provide prior to taking the extreme measure of terminating his parental rights. Finally, the father's incarceration did not per se constitute a "disability" under Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 5-313(d)(1)(i) (1989) and justify the termination of his or her parental rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment terminating the father's parental rights was reversed.

Lemley v. Lemley


No. 259, September Term, 1994


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


102 Md. App. 266; 649 A.2d 1119; 1994 Md. App. LEXIS 156



October 31, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Montgomery County. William P. Turner, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT WITH REGARD TO ABSOLUTE DIVORCE, CUSTODY AND A MONETARY AWARD VACATED AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. JUDGMENT WITH REGARD TO CHILD SUPPORT REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR AN AWARD CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN ALL OTHER RESPECTS. COSTS TO BE PAID ONE HALF BY APPELLANT AND ONE HALF BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which found in favor of appellee wife and denied the husband's exceptions to its ruling.


OVERVIEW: Appellant husband filed a petition for divorce against appellee wife. The trial court granted the wife's complaint for absolute divorce, awarded custody to the wife, and ordered the husband to pay child support. The husband then filed extensive exceptions pro se which the trial court denied. On review, the husband argued that the chancellor erred when he made no specific findings concerning the husband's exceptions. The court found that the chancellor did not address each challenge separately, nor did he state for the record how he resolved each challenge. The court found that at a minimum, the chancellor was required to summarize briefly the evidence in the record that supported each challenged fact. Therefore, because the chancellor failed to state how he resolved each challenge to the master's findings of fact, the matter was remanded for a more definite statement of his decision.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision was remanded. The trial court erred when in rejected appellant husband's exceptions to the court's ruling in favor of appellee wife without explaining the basis for the court's decision.

 

1012 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Ocean City Bd. of Supervisors of Elections v. Gisriel


No. 21, September Term, 1994


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


102 Md. App. 136; 648 A.2d 1091; 1994 Md. App. LEXIS 153



October 28, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Circuit Court of Worcester County. Theodore R. Eschenburg, Judge.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR WORCESTER COUNTY WITH DIRECTION THAT IT ENTER AN ORDER AFFIRMING THE DECISION OF THE CITY COUNCIL OF OCEAN CITY; APPELLEE TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee citizen filed a petition for referendum on the zoning ordinance. Appellant elections board rejected the petition and appellant city council affirmed the denial of the petition. The citizen appealed the city council's decision to the Circuit Court of Worcester County (Maryland), which decided that the city's refusal to strike unqualified but registered voters from the rolls was arbitrary and capricious. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The citizen, who was displeased with the city's newly enacted rezoning scheme, circulated a petition for referendum. The citizen submitted a list of names of people who he thought should be purged from the city's voter registration list because they were registered voters although they were not qualified voters. In order to get the zoning law submitted to the voters, the petition was required to contain the signatures of at least 20 percent of qualified voters in the city. The citizen's petition contained only 19 percent. The citizen contended that the board failed to purge from the registration list the names of people who were not qualified to vote. The court agreed that a registered voter was not the same as a qualified voter. However, the court held that the voter registration list on the date that the petition was filed was conclusive proof of the number of qualified voters in the city. The court thought that permitting challenges to the voter registration list anytime after the petition was filed would have created an administrative nightmare. Furthermore, the court reasoned that the statute afforded the citizen with a specific remedy to challenge the registration list.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision that the city's refusal to strike unqualified but registered voters from the rolls was arbitrary and capricious. The court remanded the case to the trial court with directions that it enter an order that affirmed the city council's denial of the citizen's petition.

 

1013 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


North Amber Meadows Homeowners Ass'n v. Haut Enters.


No. 1791, SEPTEMBER TERM, 1993


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


101 Md. App. 452; 647 A.2d 127; 1994 Md. App. LEXIS 130



September 6, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Frederick County. Mary Ann Stepler, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; CASE REMANDED FOR ENTRY OF A DECLARATORY JUDGMENT CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; APPELLEES TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, licensee and city, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Frederick County (Maryland), which entered summary judgment in favor of appellee licensor for the licensor's claims for trespass and inverse condemnation and entered a summary judgment in favor of the licensee as to the licensor's nuisance claim. The trial court ordered the licensee to reconfigure the disputed pond. The licensor also brought a cross-appeal.


OVERVIEW: The licensee and licensor owned adjacent properties that contained a water management pond that the licensor wanted to remove from his portion of the property. The city denied a grading permit to fill the licensor's portion of the pond because it was not in conformance with the approved site plan. The licensor then revoked the license to have the pond occupy a part of the licensor's property. The licensor sought declaratory relief and damages, and the trial court found that the city's denial of the grading permit amounted to an unconstitutional taking. The court reversed, finding that the trial judge erred in concluding that the city was liable for taking by inverse condemnation where the taking occurred when the licensor revoked the license with no governmental action taken. Thus, the city was not liable for paying the relocation costs, and the licensee was not required to remove the pond upon revocation of the license. The court found there was no taking by the city under inverse condemnation or police power because the permit was denied as inconsistent with the approved site plan and none of the city's actions constituted a taking of any kind.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded for the entry of a declaratory judgment in favor of the city and licensee.

 

1014 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


In re Adoption/Guardianship No. 2633


No. 1638, September Term, 1993


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


101 Md. App. 274; 646 A.2d 1036; 1994 Md. App. LEXIS 126



September 2, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: The Name of this Case has been Corrected by the Court September 8, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Washington County. Daniel W. Moylan, JUDGE



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE WASHINGTON COUNTY DEPARTMENT OF SOCIAL SERVICES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated adoption and civil rights action, appellant foster parents challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Washington County (Maryland), that denied their petition for adoption of an African-American toddler, in favor of appellee Washington County Department of Social Services (WCDSS), entered an adoption decree in favor of an African-American couple, and dismissed the foster parents' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 civil rights action.


OVERVIEW: The lower court denied a petition by foster parents, a Caucasian couple, for adoption of an African-American toddler, and entered an adoption decree in favor of an African-American couple, who had custody of the child's two older brothers, and dismissed the foster parents' civil rights action. On appeal, the court agreed with the lower court that neither the foster parents nor the child had a constitutionally protected liberty interest in preserving the foster family unit. The foster parents claimed that the trial court abused its discretion because they were preferred under Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 5-525(c)(3). The court disagreed, finding the statute in no way mandated placement with foster parents. The court found the WCDSS did not reject the foster parents because they were Caucasian, it selected the other family because it was a highly suitable African-American family that already had custody of the child's siblings. The court held that although the trial court erred by finding that the foster parents' constitutional claims were without merit, the error was harmless because, at the time it considered the motion, the foster parents were left without any discernible remedy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision below and concluded that the child should remain in her current adoptive placement with the African-American family. The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the civil rights action as well. The court held that costs were to be paid by the WCDSS.

 

1015 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Manders v. Brown


No. 1893, September Term, 1993


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


101 Md. App. 191; 643 A.2d 931; 1994 Md. App. LEXIS 116



July 5, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Somerset County. Richard D. Warren, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: ORDER OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR SOMERSET COUNTY VACATED AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID ONE-HALF BY APPELLEES AND ONE-HALF BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of orders of the Circuit Court for Somerset County (Maryland), which granted the motion of appellees, city councilmen and mayor, to dismiss the landowner's complaint for misrepresentation and misuse of public funds, which denied the landowner's motion for recusal of the trial judge and which granted the councilmen and mayor's motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The landowner operated a shipyard located in the city, which was represented by the councilmen and the mayor. After a fire destroyed two city blocks adjacent to the shipyard, the councilmen and the mayor saw an opportunity for an urban redevelopment plan for the area. As such, they informed the landowner that his shipyard was inconsistent with the plan to rezone the area from commercial to tourist/maritime. The landowner alleged that the councilmen and the mayor fraudulently and with malice violated Crisfield, Md., City Code art. III, § C13-5(A) when they modified the urban renewal plan without holding a public meeting. The councilmen and the mayor argued that they were immune to the action as legislators. The court vacated the order dismissing the complaint and remanded because the record was incomplete as to whether the councilmen restricted their functions to the traditional roles of speech and debate protected during legislative deliberations or to actions indirectly required to carry on those deliberations. However, the court affirmed the trial court's orders granting a new trial and denying the landowner's motion to recuse the trial judge.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment dismissing the landowner's complaint and remanded for further proceedings. However, the court affirmed the grant of the motion for a new trial and the denial of the motion to recuse the trial judge.

 

1016 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Vieira v. Prince George's County


No. 1480, September Term, 1993


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


101 Md. App. 220; 645 A.2d 639; 1994 Md. App. LEXIS 94



June 8, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Prince George's County. Darlene G. Perry, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO ENTER AN ORDER CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. APPELLEE TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, individual seeking recovery of seized money, challenged an order from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which ordered forfeiture of appellant's money in an action filed by appellees, county and its finance director.


OVERVIEW: Appellees instituted a forfeiture action against appellant for money seized following a traffic stop during which appellant was found in possession of drug paraphernalia. Appellant filed a petition for the seized money, alleging that appellees failed to file the requisite show cause order within 90 days following the disposition of the underlying criminal proceeding pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 297(d)(2)(i) (1992). The trial court denied the petition and appellant sought review. The court reversed and remanded the judgment. The court held that appellees failed to comply with statutory law by filing a complaint without the requisite executed show cause order within the 90-day period because although Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 297(d)(2), (3)(i) stated only that the proceeding had to have been "instituted" within the 90-day period, the provisions had to be read in harmony with Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 297(d)(2)(i), which required applications be made by complaint, affidavit, and the show cause order. The court found that to have held otherwise, appellant would not have been able to petition for the return as required by Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 297(d)(3)(i).


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded an order denying appellant's petition for the recovery of money in appellees' forfeiture action.

 

1017 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Lussier v. Maryland Racing Comm'n


No. 1461, September Term, 1993


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


100 Md. App. 190; 640 A.2d 259; 1994 Md. App. LEXIS 70



April 29, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 19, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore County. James T. Smith, Jr., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. APPELLANT TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant race horse owner (owner) sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which affirmed the decision of appellee, the Maryland Racing Commission (commission), fining the owner for violating commission regulations.


OVERVIEW: The commission concluded, after an investigation, that the owner had violated the commission's regulations by, inter alia, participating in improper acts in relation to racing, transferring two horses from himself to the name of another person for a purpose other than the legitimate sale of a horse, and engaging in conduct detrimental to racing. The commission fined the owner, and he appealed to the circuit court, which, after conducting a hearing, affirmed the decision of the commission. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that (1) the legislative grant of authority to regulate racing included the power to fine those general licensees who violated the commission's regulations; (2) there was clear and convincing, albeit largely circumstantial, evidence to support the commission's conclusions regarding the owner's wrongdoing; (3) the phrases "participating in an improper act related to racing" and "conduct detrimental to racing" were not unconstitutionally vague; and (4) the owner waived any complaint he might have had as to out-of-state enforcement of the commission's subpoena by appearing at the hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court, which affirmed the commission's decision to fine the owner for violating commission regulations. The court also held that the owner was to pay costs.

Ajamian v. Montgomery County


No. 88, September Term, 1994


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


99 Md. App. 665; 639 A.2d 157; 1994 Md. App. LEXIS 55



April 4, 1994, Decided  
April 4, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Montgomery County. Vincent Ferretti, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which rejected their challenges to a redistricting plan enacted by defendant county.


OVERVIEW: The objecting citizens alleged a violation of the Open Meetings Act, Md. Code Ann. State Gov't. §§ 10-501 to 10-512 (1984), and also claimed that certain amendments to the redistricting ordinance were improperly adopted. The court held that the attendance of council members at a meeting held by a political group did not violate the Open Meetings Act because, although the redistricting plan was discussed, the council members did not transact public business at the private meeting. The court held that the amendments did not require additional publication or public hearings because they were not substantial or material. The court held that allegations of political gerrymandering did not raise federal equal protection concerns because no election had yet been held under the new system; hence, there was no evidence of actual discriminatory effect on any group.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that approved the redistricting plan.

Purohit v. State


No. 868, September Term, 1993


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


99 Md. App. 566; 638 A.2d 1206; 1994 Md. App. LEXIS 53



March 31, 1994, Decided  
March 31, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Allegany County. Gary G. Leasure, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court for Allegany County (Maryland) that convicted him of possession with intent to distribute, and distribution of, obscene matter.


OVERVIEW: After his conviction of possession with intent to distribute, and distribution of, obscene matter, defendant sought review based on three issues included whether defendant was entitled to introduce videotapes of a similar nature that were distributed by local merchants, whether defendant was entitled to have the jury consider the defense of discriminatory prosecution, and whether the prosecutor's remarks during closing argument necessitated a mistrial. In affirming, the court held that defendant did not make a sufficient proffer of the contents of the videotapes to allow an appeal on that issue. The court further held that it was not within the province of the jury to consider the issue of discriminatory prosecution. The court held that a criminal defendant who claimed that the State instituted criminal proceedings in violation of the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment had to raise that issue pre-trial for resolution by the court. Finally, the court held that the State's remark regarding animals, even if improper, was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court and found that the conviction of defendant was proper.

Maryland Aviation Admin. v. Newsome


No. 1952, September Term, 1992


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


99 Md. App. 269; 637 A.2d 469; 1994 Md. App. LEXIS 33



February 23, 1994, Decided  
February 23, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County. Robert H. Heller, Jr., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY REVERSING THE BOARD OF AIRPORT ZONING APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Maryland Aviation Administration (MAA), challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which reversed the decision of the Maryland Department of Transportation Board of Airport Zoning Appeals that denied appellee builder a variance to permit the construction of 27 houses.


OVERVIEW: One of the reasons given for the Board's denial of the variance was that the number of persons who would be affected by high levels of noise was estimated to be about 68, and the density of the proposed individual building lots would be substantially greater than the low density developed in the surrounding residential community. In affirming, the court held that the trial court properly determined that the Board exceeded its authority in determining that the variance should be denied because of the increase in density. While it was not always easy to determine what was a question of law and what was a question of fact, it seemed to the court that whether the Board was empowered to consider the question of density was purely a question of law. Thus, the trial court was free to substitute its judgment for that of the Board. Although it would have been within the purview of the Board to determine that a variance should not be granted, that determination could not be based upon the anticipated increase in density. The court's decision was bottomed on an erroneous legal conclusion, i.e., that the density was a proper consideration for determining whether to grant or deny the variance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Davis v. Mayor of Annapolis


No. 559, September Term, 1993


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


98 Md. App. 707; 635 A.2d 36; 1994 Md. App. LEXIS 10



January 5, 1994, Decided  
January 5, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County. Lawrence H. Rushworth, Jr., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO THE TRIAL COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) that denied his petition for mandamus with respect to the disability retirement board's denial of his application for disability benefits.


OVERVIEW: The police officer applied to the disability retirement board (board) to determine his ability to function as a police officer and for disability benefits. At the time the police officer was injured, the applicable city ordinance provided for disability benefits based on permanent incapacity from active service. A subsequent ordinance changed the applicable standard to a permanent incapacity from engaging in any occupation or from performing any job in the police department. The board applied the subsequent standard and denied the police officer's application. The trial court then denied the police officer's petition for mandamus. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case in order for the board to reconsider the police officer's claims under the standard in effect at the time of his injury. The court ruled that the ordinance in effect at the time of the injury was applicable. The court determined that the police officer's contractual rights to disability benefits vested under his previous pension contract prior to the adoption of the new ordinance and that the new ordinance applied only prospectively to disability rights that had not yet arisen.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's judgment that denied the police officer's petition for mandamus with respect to the board's denial of his application for disability benefits. The court remanded the case to the trial court and directed the trial court to remand the case to the board with directions to reconsider the police officer's claim using the standard in effect at the time of his injury.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) that found in favor of appellee taxpayers that a development impact tax was invalid.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers sought a judgment finding the county's development impact tax to be invalid. After an adverse decision from the tax court, the taxpayers challenged the decision in the lower court, which found the tax to be invalid. In reversing, the court held that the county had the power to impose impact taxes, despite the fact that the statute actually imposing them recited an inapplicable statutory source of power. The court further found that the development impact tax was an excise tax, and not a tax on intangible property, that the county had the authority to enact. The tax was not a tax on ownership, but instead was a tax on the use of property. The court also held that the classification between new and existing development was rational and did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment from the lower court and found that the development impact tax was valid.

Thomas v. State

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Somerset County (Maryland), which merged his crimes, including assault and battery to a prison guard, for purposes of sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was in custody and was accused of violating a prison rule. Defendant was then brought before a prison guard for a hearing. The guard found him guilty of violating the prison rule. At sentencing the trial court merged defendant's crimes for sentencing purposes and sentenced him to 10 years. On review, defendant argued that the sentence was disproportionate to the crime. The court reasoned that defendant's crimes were serious and that attacking a prison guard was not to be tolerated in order to maintain prison discipline. Therefore, defendant's sentence was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision was affirmed.

Miller v. State


No. 1231, September Term, 1993


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


98 Md. App. 634; 635 A.2d 1; 1993 Md. App. LEXIS 193



December 29, 1993, Decided  
December 29, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Opinion Corrected January 26, 1994. Certiorari Granted March 11, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Howard County. Raymond J. Kane, Jr., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: ORDER OF AUGUST 17, 1993 REVERSED; STATE TO PROVIDE THROUGH OFFICE OF PUBLIC DEFENDER TRANSCRIPT AND OTHER DOCUMENTS PURSUANT TO MD.RULES 1-325 AND 8-505; COSTS OF THIS PROCEEDING TO BE PAID BY HOWARD COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Howard County (Maryland), which denied his motion to require the State to provide him with a free transcript of the trial proceeding for use in his appeal following his conviction for a number of offenses, including felony murder. At trial, defendant, who was indigent, declined an offer of representation by the public defender's office. Instead, defendant privately retained his own counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's counsel asserted at oral argument that he continued to represent defendant without charge to him, on a pro bono basis. There was no dispute that defendant was unable by reason of poverty to pay for the transcript. There was also no dispute that the public defender's office was authorized by law to represent defendant in his appeal and that it had never declined to provide that representation. Relying on Md. R. 1-325(b), the trial court refused to order the State to pay for the transcript because the public defender's office had not declined representation of defendant. In reversing, the court held that, where an indigent defendant who otherwise would qualify for representation by the public defender chose to be represented by a qualified private attorney and that attorney elected to represent defendant without fee of any kind or from any person, strictly on a pro bono basis, the public defender was obliged to provide the necessary transcript and, subject to Md. R. 8-505, pay the cost of the brief and other necessary documents as well.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order.

TIDEWATER/HAVRE DE GRACE, INC. v. MAYOR & CITY COUNCIL OF HAVRE DE GRACE


No. 461, September Term, 1993


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


98 Md. App. 218; 632 A.2d 509; 1993 Md. App. LEXIS 167



November 4, 1993, Decided  
November 4, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Granted January 28, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: TWO APPEALS FROM THE Circuit Court for Harford County. William O. Carr, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART; CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HARFORD COUNTY WITH DIRECTIONS TO ENTER AN ORDER CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID 50% BY APPELLANTS/CROSS-APPELLEES AND 50% BY APPELLEES/CROSS-APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant marinas sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Harford County (Maryland), which upheld the validity of a local tax ordinance. Appellees, a mayor and a city, cross-appealed, contending that the trial court's interpretation of the local tax ordinance defeated the intent and purpose of its enactment.


OVERVIEW: The marinas filed an action against the city challenging the validity of a local tax ordinance that levied fees on both wet and dry storage of boats. The trial court upheld the ordinance, holding that the city had sufficient authority to pass the ordinance. On appeal, the court agreed and held that the marinas failed to provide persuasive evidence to overcome the plain meaning of the statutory language of the tax ordinance. The court found that there was nothing in the language of the ordinance that contradicted the trial court's finding that the lessees were charged with the duty of paying the fee, and the marinas were charged with the duty of collecting it and further ruled that the tax ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague. The city cross-appealed and contended that the trial court's opinion inadequately expressed the marinas' obligation under the ordinance. The court held that to the degree that the trial court suggested that a marina could permissibly collect its rental fees without incurring liability to the city for the user tax, it erred. The court found that the marinas were obligated to charge and collect the user fees at the same time it collected its rental fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that upheld the tax ordinance and reversed in part the trial court's decision that suggested that a marina could permissibly collect its rental fees without incurring liability to the city for the user tax.

Dr. K. v. State Bd. of Physician Quality Assurance


No. 138, September Term, 1993


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


98 Md. App. 103; 632 A.2d 453; 1993 Md. App. LEXIS 165



November 2, 1993, Decided  
November 2, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied March 9, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Montgomery County. Irma S. Raker, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, psychiatrist and patient, sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) denying appellants' motion to quash a subpoena or in the alternative for a protective order, and a denial of a motion for reconsideration in an investigative action by appellee State Board of Physician Quality Assurance requesting the record's relating to patient's treatment.


OVERVIEW: Appellee State Board of Physician Quality Assurance received two formal complaints that appellant psychiatrist and appellant former patient were having a romantic relationship and that appellant psychiatrist was depressed and abusing alcohol. Pursuant to its legislative authority, appellee initiated an investigation and subpoenaed appellant psychiatrist's records relating to the former patient's treatment. Appellants opposed the subpoena, contending a patient's constitutional right of privacy barred the disclosure of mental health records. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying appellants' motion to quash the subpoena or in the alternative for a protective order, and motion for reconsideration. The court held that appellant patient's constitutional right to privacy in her medical records pertaining to her treatment was outweighed by the state's compelling interest in obtaining those records for the purpose of investigating possible disciplinary action against appellant psychiatrist. The court concluded that to give appellants a veto over appellee's power to regulate licensed physicians would be to eviscerate appellee's ability to protect the larger public interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying appellant psychiatrist and patient's motion to quash a subpoena or in the alternative for a protective order, and motion for reconsideration. The court held that appellant patient's constitutional right to privacy in her medical records pertaining to her treatment by appellant psychiatrist was outweighed by the states compelling interests in obtaining those records.

First Am. Bank v. Shivers


No. 1903, September Term, 1992


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


97 Md. App. 405; 629 A.2d 1334; 1993 Md. App. LEXIS 136



September 3, 1993, Decided  
September 3, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Montgomery County. Ann S. Harrington, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of Circuit Court, Montgomery County (Maryland) granting appellee's motion for summary judgment in appellee's action alleging failure to send certified mail notice pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Corps & Ass'ns § 3-207(b), applying to bank mergers under Md. Code Ann., Fin. Inst. § 1-201.


OVERVIEW: Appellant entered into a merger with another bank. Appellee, as a dissenting shareholder voted against the merger. The merger was approved. Appellant sent, by regular mail, notice of effective date of merger to its shareholders. Dissenting shareholders had 30 days to perfect their rights. Appellee opened the notice one-day after the statutory period ended. The trial court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, appellant argued that there was no certified mail requirement in the merger provisions of Md. Code. Ann., Fin. Inst. §§ 3-701 to -721. The court disagreed, holding that the plain language of Md. Code Ann., Fin. Inst. § 1-201 compelled the conclusion that Md. Code Ann., Corps. & Ass'ns § 3-207(b) required a bank to use personal delivery or certified mail as the manner of sending notice of the effective date of a merger to the bank's shareholders.


OUTCOME: The order granting appellee's motion for summary judgment was affirmed, as appellee did not receive notice consistent with the requirements of the Maryland code.

Hof v. State


No. 952, September Term, 1992


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


97 Md. App. 242; 629 A.2d 1251; 1993 Md. App. LEXIS 131



September 1, 1993, Decided  
September 1, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 2, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore County. Leonard S. Jacobson, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which convicted him of armed robbery and a related handgun offense.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contended that the trial court erred in failing to instruct the jury adequately on the common law voluntariness of a confession. He further argued that the trial court abused its discretion when it permitted him to be escorted into the courtroom on occasions when in-court identifications were to be made, in permitting the introduction of his unsanitized mug shot, and in refusing to grant a postponement. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. It found that the jury was instructed as to every element necessary to a finding that appellant's confession was voluntary. The court held that the trial court's conduct of the in-court identifications was within its legitimate discretionary range because the essential state interests of preventing escape, protecting those in the courtroom, and maintaining order in the courtroom justified physically restraining appellant. It found no error in the mug shot's admission because a witness's selection of appellant's photograph from an array was strongly corroborative of her later in-court identification. The court could not say that the trial court abused its discretion in denying a postponement for which no need was shown.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted appellant of armed robbery and a related handgun offense.

Rossville Vending Mach. Corp. v. Comptroller of Treasury


No. 1404, September Term, 1992


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


97 Md. App. 305; 629 A.2d 1283; 1993 Md. App. LEXIS 129



September 1, 1993, Decided  
September 1, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 7, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore County. James T. Smith, Jr., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant vending machine corporation (corporation) challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which affirmed a tax court ruling that sustained an assessment for delinquent admissions and amusement taxes issued by appellee, the Comptroller of the Treasury, against the corporation.


OVERVIEW: The vending machine corporation (corporation) operated video poker machines that it placed in bars and restaurants. After an investigation, the Comptroller of the Treasury (Comptroller) found that the corporation owed admissions and amusement taxes because cash payments made to players of the amusement machines were includable as gross receipts. The circuit court affirmed the tax court's affirmance of the Comptroller's ruling. The court likewise affirmed. The court held that cash payments made to players of the amusement machines were includable as gross receipts and therefore subject to the admissions and amusement tax. Examining former Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 402, and dictionary definition of "gross receipts," the court concluded that the natural and ordinary significance of "gross receipts" as used in the context of the Maryland admissions and amusement tax statute provided no room for reasonable argument that it contemplated deductions or adjustments for expenses, partner/co-venturer reimbursements, or trade discounts before calculation of the tax due. Further, the Comptroller consistently applied his interpretation of the statute. The tax was thus properly assessed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Comptroller of the Treasury's ruling that assessed delinquent admissions and amusement taxes against the vending machine corporation.

Montgomery County v. Schooley


No. 1645, September Term, 1992


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


97 Md. App. 107; 627 A.2d 69; 1993 Md. App. LEXIS 122



July 8, 1993, Decided  
July 8, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Montgomery County. DeLawrence Beard, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: ORDER DENYING MOTION FOR PROTECTIVE ORDER VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS; APPELLANTS AND APPELLEES TO PAY THEIR OWN COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which denied appellant's motion for a protective order blocking appellees, individuals, requested deposition of a member of appellant's council.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, individuals, challenged the councilmanic redistricting plan adopted by appellant county's council following the 1990 census. This action concerned discovery that arose during the litigation. Appellees sought to take the deposition of a member of appellant's council. Appellant filed a motion for a protective order blocking that deposition. The lower court denied the motion and the court vacated that order and remanded the case to the lower court for further proceedings. The court stated that appellant did have standing under R. 2-403(a) to invoke the privilege on behalf of the other members of council. The court concluded that appellees maintained that there were areas of inquiry that could lead to admissible evidence, even though the court could not ascertain from the record what they could be. To a large extent, the areas of permissible inquiry under Md. R. Civ. P. 2-402 could overlap those that could be permissible under the privilege. The court permitted appellees to establish their entitlement to depose the member under the rule.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decision of the lower court in favor of appellees, individuals, and against appellant county because appellant had standing to invoke legislative privilege on behalf of council members. On remand, appellees were permitted to attempt to establish their entitlement to depose the council member under the rules of civil procedure.

Gilchrist v. State


No. 1594, September Term, 1992


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


97 Md. App. 55; 627 A.2d 44; 1993 Md. App. LEXIS 119



July 6, 1993, Decided  
July 6, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 13, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore City. Ellen M. Heller, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which convicted defendant of distribution of cocaine and possession of cocaine with intent to distribute. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in striking the jury panel and beginning jury selection anew based on a finding that defense counsel had discriminatorily used peremptory strikes to exclude white members of the jury panel.


OVERVIEW: During the jury selection process, the prosecuting attorney expressed her concern that defense counsel was exercising the use of her peremptory strikes in a racially biased manner by excluding white venire persons. The trial court conducted a colloquy with defense counsel and determined that defense counsel had misused peremptory strikes for an improper purpose, discharged the venire and began the jury selection process anew. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court held that the Batson analysis applied equally to a defendant's use of peremptory strikes, that the Batson analysis protected against removal of white persons from the jury as well as black persons, and that the trial court properly made a determination that defense counsel used her peremptory strikes in a discriminatory manner and properly resolved the problem by discharging the venire and impaneling a new venire, which in effect, granted the prosecution a new trial. The court also found that defendant was not prejudiced by the ultimate selection of a jury from the second venire.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1033 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Offen v. County Council


No. 1445, September Term, 1992


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


96 Md. App. 526; 625 A.2d 424; 1993 Md. App. LEXIS 86



May 3, 1993  
May 3, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 29, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Prince George's County. Steven I. Platt, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT UPHOLDING COMPREHENSIVE REZONING AFFIRMED; TRIAL COURT'S JUDGMENT OTHERWISE VACATED AND CASE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE PAID BY PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland) affirming the comprehensive rezoning plan adopted by appellee county council; determining that the county's actions before the adoption of this plan concerning the owner's commercially-zoned property for a sewer development were not illegal, arbitrary, or capricious; and holding that the owner had no vested rights in the prior zoning.


OVERVIEW: The owner contested the circuit court decision that (1) sustained the comprehensive rezoning plan approved by the county; (2) upheld the county's actions, before the approval of the comprehensive rezoning, regarding the property owner's commercially-zoned property for a planned sewer development as not illegal, arbitrary, or capricious; and (3) held that the owner had no vested rights in the previous zoning. The court affirmed the first judgment sustaining the comprehensive rezoning. The court vacated and remanded the cause on all other issues to continue the proceedings based on the opinion, with costs to the county. The court found that the "takings" issue was ripe for determination. The court held that no substantive changes had occurred in federal or state law to permit the regulation of uses, as long as all economically viable uses were not prohibited. The court held that zoning estoppel applied in Maryland. The court did found that zoning estoppel could have resulted from the county's actions that delayed appellant's ability to obtain building permits and to begin construction, and that these circumstances could establish in the owner a vested interest in the prior zoning.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the circuit court decision challenged by the owner involving the comprehensive rezoning plan accepted by the county. The court vacated and remanded the matter on the holding that the county's actions before the acceptance of that plan respecting the owner's commercially-zoned property for the sewer development were not illegal, arbitrary, or capricious; and that the owner lacked vested rights in the prior zoning.

Strother v. Board of Educ.


No. 1074, September Term, 1992


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


96 Md. App. 99; 623 A.2d 717; 1993 Md. App. LEXIS 82



April 30, 1993  
April 30, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Howard County. James B. Dudley, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HOWARD COUNTY VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS THAT IT REVERSE THE DECISIONS OF THE MARYLAND STATE BOARD OF EDUCATION AND REMAND THESE APPEALS TO THE STATE BOARD FOR CONSIDERATION OF THE MERITS; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public school teachers sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Howard County (Maryland), which affirmed the determination of appellee state board of education that the teachers' challenges to unfavorable classroom observation reports were not appealable in favor of appellee county board.


OVERVIEW: The teachers received written performance reports from their superiors that were less than satisfactory. The teachers filed a grievance. The county board received an order from the circuit court staying the arbitration proceedings pending exhaustion of their administrative remedies. The teachers appealed to the state board, which remanded to the county board. The county board determined that classroom observation reports were not a decision made nor a controversy or dispute under Md. Code Ann., Educ. § 4-205(c) and, therefore, were not appealable. The teachers appealed to the state board, which held that disputed classroom observations were not appealable. The teachers appealed to the circuit court, which affirmed the decision of the state board. The teachers sought review and the court vacated the circuit court's judgment and remanded the case. The court held the state board had determined that the resolution of disputes involving classroom observation reports were within the authority of and to be decided by the local superintendent. Thus, the superintendent's decision was appealable by the affected teacher to the county board and the state board.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the circuit court and remanded the case to the circuit court with directions that it reverse the decisions of the state board and remand the appeals to the state board for consideration on the merits. The court ordered costs to be paid by the county board.

Pruitt v. Howard County Sheriff's Dep't


No. 1086, September Term, 1992


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


96 Md. App. 60; 623 A.2d 696; 1993 Md. App. LEXIS 77



April 29, 1993  
April 29, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied September 15, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County. Eugene M. Lerner, JUDGE

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, sheriff department officers, sought review of judgment which upheld defendant city's termination decision under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 733 (1957, 1992 Repl. Vol.) in the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland).


OVERVIEW: The sheriff's department officers sought review of a judgment which upheld the city's termination decision under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 733 (1957, 1992 Repl. Vol.), contending they were improperly fired by for misconduct. The sheriff's department officers urged that their actions, which included parodies of Hogan's Heroes, exaggerated Germans, and the Hitler hand salute constituted First Amendment free speech. The court affirmed the judgment, finding the termination of the sheriff's department officers for such conduct did not infringe upon a public employees' constitutionally protected free speech under the requisite balance between the interests of the public employee as a citizen in commenting upon matters of public concern and the interest of the state as an employer in promoting the efficiency of public services. The court found the sheriff's department officers' speech did not address a matter of public concern that would have entitled it to constitutional protection. The court observed the sheriff's department officers conduct was humorous in nature and intended as a joke rather than the presentation of issues of public community concern.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment which upheld the city's decision to terminate the sheriff's department officers' employment.

Esslinger v. Baltimore City


No. 1125, September Term, 1992


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


95 Md. App. 607; 622 A.2d 774; 1993 Md. App. LEXIS 67



April 5, 1993, Decided  
April 5, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore City. John N. Prevas, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART. CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID ONE HALF BY APPELLANT AND ONE HALF BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowner challenged the judgment of Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) that dismissed appellant's complaint under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 against respondent zoning board for repeated denial of appellant's requests to put a satellite dish on his property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant homeowner made several attempts to gain permission from respondent zoning board to put a satellite dish on his property. The first denial was appealed and affirmed, the second denial was not appealed. On appeal from the third denial the lower court granted summary judgment to respondent holding that the Satellite Dish Ordinance, Baltimore City Code art. 30, was not preempted by 47 C.F.R. § 25.104 (1986). Appellant's complaint under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 was dismissed. The court affirmed in part finding that appellant's constitutional claims were barred by res judicata where the same parties were involved in the lawsuit and the zoning case, in which there was a final judgment, the claims arose from the same transaction, and appellant could have raised the constitutional claims in court as a means of reversing the adverse zoning decision. The court reversed in part finding that his damages claims were not barred by res judicata because he could not have raised them on review of the zoning case, and collateral estoppel was inapplicable where relitigation was necessary to account for a change in the applicable legal context and to avoid inequitable administration of the laws.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing appellant homeowner's civil rights action against respondent zoning board was affirmed in part because the constitutional claims were barred by res judicata when they arose from the same transaction and could have been raised on review of the zoning decision. The judgment was reversed in part because collateral estoppel did not bar the claim for damages where relitigation was necessary to account for a change in the law.

Levinson v. Montgomery County

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant doctor challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which affirmed the decision of appellee Montgomery County Board of Appeals (board) upholding the Montgomery County Department of Environmental Protection's (DEP) notice of zoning violation issued to the doctor.


OVERVIEW: The doctor, an ophthalmologist, set up his ophthalmology practice from the basement of his home. The doctor maintained an office and an optical dispensary from which eyeglasses were sold. Maryland State Dep't of Pub. Safety & Correctional Servs. v. Bailey

COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


95 Md. App. 12; 619 A.2d 176; 1993 Md. App. LEXIS 35; 143 L.R.R.M. 2353



January 29, 1993, Decided  
January 29, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore County. J. William Hinkel, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state correctional services sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which granted appellee supervisor the right to represent non-supervisory employees in grievance procedures.


OVERVIEW: The supervisor, before becoming a supervisor over lower-level correctional officers, represented employees in grievance proceedings within the department of corrections. When the supervisor was told that he could no longer represent employees at grievance, suspension appeal, or discharge hearings, he filed a grievance petition under the state employee grievance procedures, Md. Ann. Code art. 64A, §§ 52-57 (1988). An administrative law judge held that the supervisor did not have standing to bring suit. The trial court reversed on the grounds that the order was premised on an erroneous conclusion of the law. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the supervisor failed to allege that he had been aggrieved and, thus, he lacked standing under § 53(b) because supervisors did not have a right to act as representatives. That section of the statute permitting aggrieved employees the right to representation of their choice was not meant to interfere with management's ability to make policy decisions limiting the role of its supervisors in the context of management-employee disputes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment because the supervisor lacked standing to raise the claim presented.

Warfel v. Brady


No. 546, September Term, 1992


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


95 Md. App. 1; 619 A.2d 171; 1993 Md. App. LEXIS 32



January 28, 1993, Decided  
January 28, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County. Lawrence H. Rushworth, Jr., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellants, personal representatives of the decedent's estate, sought review from an order of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which dismissed the appellants' amended complaint against the appellee personal representative for the tortfeasor, in an assault and battery suit.


OVERVIEW: The decedent died from an assault and battery. The appellants, personal representatives of the decedent, attempted to file a personal injury suit against the tortfeasor, seeking damages and a lis pendens against his real property. The complaint was defective and not properly served. The tortfeasor died and the appellee personal representative published a notice to creditors to warn that claims had to be filed within nine months of the tortfeasor's death or two months after notice. The appellants filed an amended complaint. The appellee's motion for summary judgment was denied, but a motion to dismiss was granted. On review, the court held that: (1) the trial court was not precluded from granting the appellee's motion to dismiss based on the denial of the summary judgment motion and the law of the case doctrine; (2) the doctrine of lis pendens did not apply because the complaint did not involve the tortfeasor's property; (3) the appellee was not provided sufficient notice of the appellants' claim, and therefore, did not know to consider them creditors under Md. Code § 7-103.1(a); and (5) pursuant to Md. Code § 8-104(d), the appellants' claim was untimely.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed dismissal of the personal injury suit filed by the appellants, personal representatives of the decedent's estate, against the appellee, personal representative of the tortfeasor.
