Ohio Casualty Ins. Co. v. Hallowell


No. 409, September Term, 1992


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


94 Md. App. 444; 617 A.2d 1134; 1993 Md. App. LEXIS 13



January 7, 1993  
January 7, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Orphans' Court for Howard County. Rosemary M. Ford, Catherine Waters and Charles Coles, JUDGES



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE ORPHANS' COURT DENYING APPELLANT'S CLAIM REVERSED; ORDERS AWARDING ATTORNEYS' FEES REVERSED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurer appealed from a judgment of the Orphans' Court for Howard County (Maryland), which denied the insurer's claim against defendant estate on limitations grounds. The insurer also challenged the award of legal fees to the attorney for the estate and to the attorney for the legatees.


OVERVIEW: The insurer argued that the notice provision denied it due process. The court disagreed and concluded that the statute was a self-executing limitation statute. Thus, due process concerns were not implicated, and the statute was not unconstitutional. However, the court determined that the parties entered into an express agreement extending the limitation period. In doing so, the period was waived. The court held that personal representatives could waive the application of the statute of limitation, and that when the orphans' court denied the insurer's claim, it erred.


OUTCOME: Judgment denying the insurer's claim on limitations grounds was reversed. The orders awarding attorney fees to the estate were reversed.

State v. Lee


No. 568, September Term, 1992


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


93 Md. App. 408; 613 A.2d 395; 1992 Md. App. LEXIS 179



September 30, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Allegany County. Gary G. Leasure, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Allegany County (Maryland), which granted defendant's motion to suppress as evidence certain items, including controlled dangerous substances, drug paraphernalia, and money, that were seized and removed from his home by virtue of a search and seizure warrant.


OVERVIEW: The State suggested that the issue before the court was whether the use of anticipatory warrants should have been sanctioned in Maryland. The court declined to frame the issue in that manner and held that the case involved only the question of whether the trial court erred in ruling that the specific warrant in question, authorizing and directing a search of defendant's residence, was invalid. The court found that even if anticipatory warrants were not per se violative of the Fourth Amendment, the warrant in the case was invalid. The warrant was invalid because there was at the time of issuance no probable cause to believe, only speculation, that at some point in time a transaction would have occurred that would have demonstrated the existence of contraband in the premises to be searched and that it was left to the unrestricted judgment of the executing officer to determine whether the triggering event, a "verified buy," had occurred. Therefore, the court concluded that the anticipatory warrant for the search of defendant's home was invalid because it was issued without probable cause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1043 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Shrivastava v. Mates


No. 1796, September Term, 1991


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


93 Md. App. 320; 612 A.2d 313; 1992 Md. App. LEXIS 232



September 8, 1992 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS IN ACCORDANCE WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother filed a petition for modification of child support based on the adoption of the Maryland child support guidelines (the guidelines), Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 12-201 et seq. (1991). The mother challenged an order the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) that denied her motion, concluded that use of the guidelines would have been unjust and inappropriate, and dismissed the case without prejudice.


OVERVIEW: Appellee father alleged that application of the guidelines would have unconstitutionally impaired the divorce settlement agreement obligation. The mother argued that there was insufficient evidence that application of the guidelines would have been unjust or inappropriate, and that insufficient findings were made to justify a departure from the guidelines. The court held that the guidelines were reasonable and appropriate for their significant and legitimate public purpose. The parties could not contractually bind the circuit court to a certain amount of child support. Because application of the guidelines resulted in a change in the child support obligation of more than 25 percent there was a rebuttable presumption that the guidelines' adoption was a material change in circumstances requiring modification of the child support obligation. The presumption was not automatically rebutted by a finding that strict application of the guidelines was unjust or inappropriate. Even had such a finding been made the mother was still entitled to consideration of her request. The circuit court was required to show how any deviation from the guidelines served the best interests of the children.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the motion to modify child support was reversed and the case was remanded.

Medical Mut. Liability Ins. Soc. v. B. Dixon Evander & Assoc., Inc.


No. 1752, September Term, 1991


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


92 Md. App. 551; 609 A.2d 353; 1992 Md. App. LEXIS 144



July 13, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore City. David Ross, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: PUNITIVE DAMAGE AWARDS VACATED. JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN ALL OTHER RESPECTS. CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID ONE HALF BY APPELLANTS AND ONE HALF BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, insurer and officer, challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which entered a jury verdict in favor of appellee insurance broker on his claims of tortious interference with business relationships. The jury awarded $ 1.725 million in compensatory damages and $ 5 million and $ 2 million in punitive damages against the insurer and the officer, respectively.


OVERVIEW: An insurance broker acted independently, selling medical malpractice insurance for an insurer, as well as for the insurer's competitor. The insurer objected to this behavior and distributed a letter to the broker's clients that terminated their relationship with the broker and implied that the broker had done something improper. The court on appeal held that the broker presented sufficient evidence of actual malice to support his claims of tortious interference, although the jury reached no verdict on defamation. The court affirmed the verdict but found that the punitive damage award had not received independent review by the trial court. For this case alone, based on the size of the punitive damage award, the court held that due process was violated and that a remand was necessary so that the trial court could consider whether the enormous sum awarded accomplished society's goals and was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the insurance broker, but vacated the award of punitive damages and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Brown v. Ashton


No. 1682 September Term, 1991


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


93 Md. App. 25; 611 A.2d 599; 1992 Md. App. LEXIS 151



July 9, 1992  
July 9, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 28, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Frederick County. G. Edward Dwyer, Jr., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED FOR ENTRY OF A DECLARATORY JUDGMENT CONSISTENT WITH DIRECTIVES SET FORTH WITHIN. COSTS TO BE PAID ONE HALF BY APPELLANTS AND ONE HALF BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, two teenagers who were detained under a juvenile curfew, challenged the constitutionality of the ordinance and alleged negligence, assault and battery, false imprisonment, invasion of privacy, and intentional infliction of emotional distress. The Circuit Court for Frederick County (Maryland) granted summary judgment to defendants, the mayor and the city, and the teenagers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The two teenagers, 16 and 19 years old, were detained under a curfew aimed at restricting the nighttime activities of people under 18. On appeal from summary judgment in favor of the mayor and the city, the court reviewed three factors that could justify differential treatment of the constitutional rights of minors: the peculiar vulnerability of children; their inability to make critical decisions in an informed, mature manner; and the importance of the parental role in child rearing. Finding that none of these factors justified the ordinance, the court concluded that the curfew burdened fundamental rights of minors and was not justified by any compelling governmental interest. The teenagers also challenged four terms of exemption as vague: "bona fide organization;" "cultural, scholastic, athletic, or recreational activity;" "supervised;" and "gainful lawful employment." The court found that the latter three terms were sufficiently self-explanatory but that "bona fide organization" was unconstitutionally vague. On the claims arising from enforcement of the ordinance, the police had probable cause for the detentions because the law was presumptively valid at the time of enforcement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment relating to the grant of summary judgment as to the common law tort claims, the federal constitutional claims, and the claims of violation of the Maryland Declaration of Rights, and reversed as to the remaining claims.

Jackson v. State


Nos. 645, 1037, September Term, 1991


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


92 Md. App. 304; 608 A.2d 782; 1992 Md. App. LEXIS 135



July 1, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 14, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] TWO APPEALS FROM THE Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County, H. Chester Goudy, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant brought a consolidated appeal to challenge his convictions by the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) in two separate cases. The trial court convicted defendant of first and second-degree sexual offenses, burglary, and assault with intent to rape in the first case, and found him guilty of assault and battery and breaking and entering in the second case.


OVERVIEW: The trial judge recanted his mistaken grant of an acquittal on the charge for assault with intent to rape and reiterated the earlier denial when defendant renewed his motion at the close of all evidence. Defendant argued that the trial judge improperly reversed himself on the acquittal and made erroneous evidentiary rulings. The court held that the trial court's withdrawal of its ruling on the felony count did not subject defendant to double jeopardy because it never entered a judgment of acquittal on the felony count or any other charge. The court reasoned that the trial judge's action was more accurately a dismissal than an acquittal because he granted defendant's motion on jurisdictional and not evidentiary grounds. The court also concluded that: (1) a proper foundation was laid for admission of the prior inconsistent statement used to impeach a defense witness; (2) the state's forensic chemistry expert was properly allowed to testify about population blood group studies upon which her opinions were based; and (3) the testimony of defendant's DNA testing expert was properly restricted in view of defendant's failure to disclose the expert's testing data and results to the state.


OUTCOME: The judgments convicting defendant of sexual offenses and burglary in one case and assault and breaking and entering in a second case were both affirmed.

Wharf at Handy's Point, Inc. v. Department of Natural Resources


No. 742, September Term, 1991


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


92 Md. App. 659; 610 A.2d 314; 1992 Md. App. LEXIS 120



May 27, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration Denied June 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Kent County, James Owen Wise, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID ONE HALF BY APPELLANT AND ONE HALF BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an owner of a wharf (owner), sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kent County (Maryland), which denied a motion of the owner to dismiss an appeal of appellee, the Chesapeake Bay Critical Area Commission (commission), seeking to reverse a county planning board's grant of final site approval of a marina to the owner.


OVERVIEW: The owner sought to develop a marina within the Chesapeake Bay Critical Area. Under a certain state act, that area was subject to protection. Although a county planning board (board) issued final site approval for the marina, the commission appealed the decision to the circuit court. The owner sought to dismiss the appeal on the ground that the commission had no statutory right to appeal. The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment. The court found that although at the time of the appeal, it was incumbent upon the commission to appeal the board's decision to a local board of appeals as directed by statute and a county zoning ordinance, such administrative remedy did not have to be exhausted prior to any judicial review of the board's decision. The court stated that a county zoning ordinance which was passed while the case was on appeal, directing that the board's decision be appealed to the circuit court, was not to be applied retroactively because the result would be the same, that is the commission would be directed to appeal the board's decision to the circuit court. Thus, the court stated that it was not required that the case be remanded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment for the commission. The court found that a county ordinance which was passed while the case was on appeal, directing that the board's decision be appealed to the circuit court, was not to be applied retroactively because the result would be the same, that is the commission would be directed to appeal the board's decision to the circuit court.

 

1050 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Hickey v. Comptroller of Treasury


No. 1202, September Term, 1991


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


92 Md. App. 1; 606 A.2d 282; 1992 Md. App. LEXIS 93



May 8, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied September 15, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Montgomery County, Vincent Ferretti, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which affirmed the tax court's denial of their claim for interest on state income tax refunds.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers, a lawyer and his wife, were residents of Maryland and paid their Maryland taxes in full each year. However, when the taxpayers discovered that they also owed taxes to New York for several years, they realized that they had overpaid their taxes to Maryland and sought a refund. While the taxpayers were paid the full amount of the refund claimed, they alleged that they were also entitled to interest on the refund. The court affirmed the denial of the taxpayers' claim for interest. The court held that the original overpayment of Maryland taxes was due to the mistake of error of the taxpayers in finding that no taxes were due to New York. Further, the taxpayers were paid their refund within 45 days of the filing of their claim, and thus, under Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 310(c), the taxpayers were not entitled to any interest on the refund. The State had no duty to pay the refund until the taxpayers' loss was claimed, and the denial of the claim for interest was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1051 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Mauk v. State


No. 1957, September Term, 1990


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


91 Md. App. 456; 605 A.2d 157; 1992 Md. App. LEXIS 89



April 29, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Dorchester County. Richard D. Warren, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Dorchester County (Maryland), denying a motion to dismiss a charge of possession of marijuana with intent to distribute on grounds of double jeopardy where defendant had been already convicted, sentenced, and punished for the offense of simple possession.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in a multi-count indictment with possession of marijuana with intent to distribute and with simple possession. There was a hung jury on the first charge and a verdict of guilty on the second. The trial court declared a mistrial on the possession with intent to distribute charge and imposed sentence on the possession conviction. After a new trial was scheduled, defendant filed a motion to dismiss on double jeopardy grounds contending that he had already been convicted for "the same offense." The trial court denied the motion. The court affirmed and held that whether the two offenses were the same for double jeopardy purposes would only apply at sentencing. The court held that defendant was not put twice in jeopardy because jeopardy had attached for both offenses at the same time and jeopardy on the intent to distribute charge was continuing. The court held that the declaration of a mistrial only suspended the jeopardy on the first charge and that retrial did not entail new jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction on the charge of possession of marijuana with intent to distribute.

 

1052 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Liberty Nursing Center, Inc. v. Department of Health & Mental Hygiene


No. 878, September Term, 1991


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


91 Md. App. 210; 603 A.2d 1344; 1992 Md. App. LEXIS 67



April 7, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 16, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore City. David B. Mitchell, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nursing home operator challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which affirmed the decision of the Nursing Home Appeals Board (NHAB) that denied reimbursement to the operator for the cost of interest associated with the purchase of the property and facilities of a nursing center from its deceased owner's estate. One of the owners of the operator purchased the center with a loan in his individual capacity.


OVERVIEW: Medicaid reimbursement to a provider, i.e. the operator, was based on certain costs incurred to operate a nursing facility. NHAB denied the operator's claim for reimbursement of interest on the owner's loan based on the related organizations principle. The operator argued that NHAB erred in disallowing the operator reimbursement for interest expenses based on that principle. In affirming, the court held that NHAB's decision was proper because: (1) the operator/owner and the deceased's estate were related organizations; (2) because the operator/owner and the estate were related organizations, no change in ownership or in capital structure between the estate and the operator/owner was recognized for purposes of reimbursement; (3) because no change in ownership or capital structure was recognized, the loan obtained by the owner was a "refinancing;" 4) refinancing was reimbursable only if it resulted in a lower cost to the State; (5) the owner's refinancing did not result in a lower cost to the State because the owner incurred mortgage debt when previously the estate had no mortgage debt; and (6) therefore, interest on the loan was not reimbursable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Bancroft Information Group, Inc. v. Comptroller of Treasury


No. 810, September Term, 1991


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


91 Md. App. 100; 603 A.2d 1289; 1992 Md. App. LEXIS 66; 20 Media L. Rep. 1016



April 6, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County. Bruce C. Williams, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE APPROPRIATE ADMINISTRATIVE AGENCY. COSTS TO BE PAID THREE-FOURTHS BY APPELLANTS AND ONE-FOURTH BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant publisher filed an action against appellee, the Comptroller of the Treasury, and claimed that Md. Regs. Code tit. 03, § 06.01.04, the sales tax regulation, was ultra vires and in violation of the First Amendment. The Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) granted the comptroller's motion to dismiss and stayed any constitutional determination pending exhaustion of administrative remedies. The publisher appealed.


OVERVIEW: The publisher published a biweekly publication. The comptroller notified the publisher that the publication did not constitute a "newspaper," under Md. Regs. Code tit. 03, § 06.01.04, and was thus subject to sales tax. Nevertheless, the publisher sought a refund for sales tax paid during the previous four quarters. The comptroller requested additional information. Instead of providing additional information, the publisher filed an action against the comptroller and claimed that the sales tax regulation was ultra vires and in violation of the First Amendment. The trial court granted the comptroller's motion to dismiss and stayed any constitutional determination pending exhaustion of administrative remedies. On review, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the requirement, in the sales tax regulation, that a newspaper be published at least once per week in order to qualify for a sales tax exemption passed constitutional muster. In addition, the court held that administrative exhaustion was required prior to judicial review of the agency action in the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to the trial court to remand the case to the appropriate administrative agency.

 

1054 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Cae-Link Corp. v. Washington Suburban Sanitary Com.


No. 849, September Term, 1991


COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS OF MARYLAND


90 Md. App. 604; 602 A.2d 239; 1992 Md. App. LEXIS 52



March 2, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] TWO APPEALS FROM THE Circuit Court for Montgomery County. Paul H. Weinstein, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT DENYING WSSC'S MOTION FOR PARTIAL SUMMARY JUDGMENT ON THE INVERSE CONDEMNATION COUNTS AGAINST CAE-LINK, BANCTEC, AND AT & T IS REVERSED; JUDGMENT ON REMAINING ISSUES VACATED; CASE REMANDED FOR NEW TRIAL; COSTS TO BE PAID 75% BY WSSC, 25% BY CAE-LINK, BANCTEC AND AT & T.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sanitary commission brought suit action against defendant landowners and the landowners counterclaimed alleging violations of nuisance and inverse condemnation. The Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) granted summary judgment in favor of the sanitary commission as to the nuisance claim, denied the motion as to the inverse condemnation claim, and denied the landowners' motion for a new trial. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: Landowners subjected to odors emanating from a composting site, which was operated by a sanitary commission, argued that the trial court erred by requiring them to prove negligence as a prerequisite to recovery on their nuisance claim. They specifically argue that in Maryland nuisance was a matter of strict liability and that negligence was not a necessary element. Landowners testified that odors from the sanitary commission's facility caused nausea and headaches. The court held that the evidence might justify a finding by the trier of fact that the odors complained of were such that they produced actual physical discomfort to persons of ordinary sensibilities, tastes, and habits, thus entitling the offended to damages. Whether the sanitary commission used state of the art facilities was irrelevant to the maintenance of the nuisance action. The court held that a nuisance existed because of a violation of an absolute duty so that it did not rest on the degree of care used. Therefore, negligence was not a necessary element of the tort of nuisance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the sanitary commission and remanded the case for a new trial.

McKay v. State


No. 285, September Term, 1991


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


90 Md. App. 204; 600 A.2d 904; 1992 Md. App. LEXIS 23



January 30, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore City. Elsbeth Bothe, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS REVERSED; CASE REMANDED FOR NEW TRIAL. COSTS TO BE PAID BY MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL OF BALTIMORE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which convicted him of assault with intent to murder, use of a handgun in the commission of a crime of violence, and carrying a handgun.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant challenged the trial judge's refusal to instruct the jury on the law of provocation. The court reversed and remanded, and held that defendant was entitled to an instruction on a hot-blooded response to legally adequate provocation. The court found, upon reviewing the record, that there was evidence from which the jury could have found that defendant acted in the heat of passion. The court determined that the evidence clearly showed that defendant successfully presented "some evidence" of heat of passion or hot blood sufficient to warrant an instruction to the jury on legally adequate provocation, even though defendant's testimony focused on the theories of perfect self-defense and imperfect self-defense. The court held that defendant met his burden of presenting sufficient evidence of mitigation to satisfy the "some evidence" test and the trial judge should have given a jury instruction as to legally adequate provocation.


OUTCOME: The convictions for assault with intent to murder, use of a handgun in the commission of a crime of violence, and carrying a handgun, were reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

Holmes v. Maryland Reclamation Assoc., Inc.


No. 2003 September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


90 Md. App. 120; 600 A.2d 864; 1992 Md. App. LEXIS 20



January 29, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Harford County. Cypert O. Whitfill, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee applicant filed an action against appellants, Harford County and Harford County Council (Council), seeking declaratory relief and alleging that the Council's decision to delete the applicant's proposed rubble landfill from the Harford County's solid waste management (SWM) plan was unconstitutional. The Circuit Court for Harford County (Maryland) granted summary judgment in favor of the applicant. The Council appealed.


OVERVIEW: After initially concluding that the applicant's request for a landfill was consistent with the SWM plan, the Council passed a resolution to delete the landfill from the SWM plan because the landfill allegedly represented a threat to the area's ground water resources. As a result, the Maryland Department of Environment (MDE) stopped processing the applicant's request for a permit. The court held that (1) Harford County was a charter home rule county and its power was limited, pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 25A, § 5(S) (1987), in those areas preempted either by the constitution, or by conflicting provisions of state law; (2) the resolution did not expressly conflict with state law, but the legislature intended to occupy the field of landfill regulation in a manner that placed certain limits on a county's role; and (3) the MDE was responsible for approving landfill sites via the permit process and neither the state legislature nor the MDE delegated that responsibility to the Council. Thus, the court held that the Council exceeded its authority in passing the resolution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

In re William George T.

January 2, 1992, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which issued an injunction barring the husband from the family home on appellee wife's motion for an ex parte injunction. The circuit court granted the injunction to keep the parties from assaulting one another upon the expiration of a district court's civil protection order that barred the husband from the family home.


OVERVIEW: Following an altercation, the husband filed a complaint for a limited divorce and the wife filed a petition for protection from domestic violence. The husband was barred from entering the family home where the wife resided. The husband was compensated for the taking by not having to provide an alternative place for the wife to live during the divorce proceedings. The court remanded the case for an immediate reconsideration of the continued need for the injunction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's issuance of an injunction barring the husband from the family home, and remanded the case for further proceedings at the earliest possible date to determine if the need for the injunction had ceased to exist.

Williams v. State


No. 326, September Term, 1991


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


89 Md. App. 685; 599 A.2d 848; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 248



December 30, 1991  
December 30, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Wicomico County. D. William Simpson, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Wicomico County (Maryland), which was entered upon a jury verdict finding him guilty of violating Maryland's drug kingpin statute, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 286 (Supp. 1991).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the statute was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to define an organizer, supervisor, manager, or financier of a drug conspiracy. The court concluded that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague because its terms were common ones and their meanings were easily ascertained and understood. The court held that defendant could not reasonably argue that he was insufficiently notified that his conduct was illegal as proscribed by the statute, nor could he argue that the statute's language provided so little guidance that the law was likely to be enforced discriminatorily. Defendant argued that the statute was overbroad because the legislature could not have intended the statute's mandatory and harsh results to apply to a courier whose only action in organizing or initiating a conspiracy was to ask a friend to accompany him on the journey to deliver the drugs. The court found that defendant mistakenly believed that he could not be convicted as a kingpin if his role was subordinate to that of another actor in the conspiracy. The court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to show that defendant managed or supervised an illicit drug operation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Anderson v. State


No. 483, September Term, 1991


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


89 Md. App. 712; 599 A.2d 861; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 253



December 30, 1991  
December 30, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 6, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore County. Leonard S. Jacobson, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED AS TO THE GUILTY FINDINGS UNDER § 286(a) FOR THE OCTOBER 18, 1989 AND OCTOBER 21, 1989 TRANSACTIONS AND UNDER § 286(f) FOR THE NOVEMBER 2, 1989 AND JANUARY 29, 1990 TRANSACTIONS. SENTENCE VACATED FOR CONVICTIONS UNDER § 286(a) FOR THE NOVEMBER 2, 1989 AND JANUARY 29, 1990 TRANSACTIONS. COSTS TO BE PAID 2/3 BY APPELLANT AND 1/3 BY BALTIMORE COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which convicted defendant of four counts of unlawful distribution of lysergic acid diethylamide (LSD) and one count of distribution of 1,000 dosage units of LSD in a case brought by the State of Maryland.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold various quantities of LSD to an undercover police detective. Defendant contended that Md. Const. art. 27, § 286(f)(1)(v), which provided a minimum sentence for distribution of dosage units of LSD, was unconstitutionally vague as to what constituted a "dosage unit" and the trial court erred in failing to merge the unlawful distribution convictions with the conviction for distributing. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to sustain the conviction under § 286(f) for distribution of 1,000 dosage units of LSD. The detective's testimony established that a dosage unit was one "hit," or the amount and form of LSD that would be sold on the street for individual use by the consumer. The statute, as applied to the facts of the case, was not unconstitutionally vague. The laboratory test results admitted into evidence proved the presence of LSD on each sheet of blotter paper and in each bottle of liquid. However, the court held that defendant's convictions for distribution were lesser-included offenses and should have merged into his five-year mandatory sentence. Thus, the court remanded the case for resentencing. The court affirmed the judgments of convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of convictions of defendant for unlawful distribution of lysergic acid diethylamide (LSD). The court remanded the case for resentencing.

White v. State


No. 193, September Term, 1991


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


89 Md. App. 590; 598 A.2d 1208; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 241



December 6, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Worcester County. Theodore R. Eschenburg, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for Worcester County (Maryland), which affirmed the judgment of the district court that quashed his subpoena for a state toxicologist to testify at his trial on charges of driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the circuit and district courts improperly failed to require the presence of the state toxicologist at trial pursuant to Md. Code Ann. Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 10-304(d) (1989) (amended Jan. 1, 1990) and that they denied his constitutional right to have compulsory process. The court affirmed. The court first addressed the fact that the circuit court heard defendant's appeal via writ of certiorari; a process by which the circuit court was supposed to determine if the district court had the right to decide what it decided, not whether it decided correctly. The court determined that the circuit court erred in this respect but, nonetheless, considered the merits of defendant's appeal. The court found that § 10-304(d) was intended to protect the public rather than benefit the defendant and that, therefore, the defendant's reliance on it was misplaced. Further, the court found that any testimony that might be offered by the toxicologist was not relevant to the issues raised by the defense and that, as a result, the quashing of the subpoena did not violate defendant's right to compulsory process or confrontation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court and that of the district court, quashing the defendant's subpoena of a state toxicologist, was affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland ) entered upon a jury verdict convicting him of willful failure to file Maryland income tax returns.


OVERVIEW: The essence of defendant's argument was that he was not required to file Maryland income tax returns or to pay any taxes because the income tax return form prescribed by the comptroller was not in compliance with the Forms Management Act (Act), Md. Code Ann., State Gov't §§ 10-604 to 10-608. He complained further that the state's witnesses and the prosecutors misled the trial court into thinking that the form was in compliance with that Act. The court held that it would matter not one whit whether the comptroller was or was not in compliance with the Act. A person was not excused from the requirement of filing a state income tax return because the form of the return was not in compliance with the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for willful failure to file Maryland income tax returns.

Thomas v. State


No. 44, September Term, 1991


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


89 Md. App. 439; 598 A.2d 789; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 231



December 2, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Montgomery County. Irma S. Raker, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; CASE REMANDED FOR NEW TRIAL; COSTS TO BE PAID BY MONTGOMERY COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which convicted defendant of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's counsel informed the trial court that defendant's interests would be best served by a bench trial rather than a jury trial. The trial court did not explain to defendant his right to a jury trial and did not make any meaningful inquiry of defendant as to his ability to understand his rights. Rather, the trial court summarily found that defendant was unable to make a knowledgeable decision concerning whether to have a bench trial or jury trial and ordered a jury trial. The primary issue on appeal was whether the trial court judge failed to afford defendant an adequate opportunity to elect between a jury trial and a bench trial. The court reversed the conviction, holding that the trial court did not afford defendant an opportunity to waive his right to a jury trial and thus to assert his right to a bench trial. This failure deprived defendant of his right to choose a bench trial. under Md. R. 4-246.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case for a new trial.

Richardson v. State


No. 124, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


89 Md. App. 259; 598 A.2d 1; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 216



November 6, 1991, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County; William M. Nickerson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED. APPELLANT TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder and robbery in the first degree by the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland). Defendant challenged his conviction and sentence claiming multiple assignments of error.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for murder and robbery in the first degree. Defendant received a life sentence for the crime of murder and a sentence of twenty years for the crime of robbery in the first degree. On review, defendant claimed that the trial court erred when it denied his pretrial motion to strike the intention to seek the death penalty. Essentially, defendant argued that under Md. Ann. Code art. 27 § 412(f)(1) the death penalty could not be sought against him because he was retarded. The court rejected this argument finding that the determination of whether defendant was retarded or not was to be made at the sentencing stage rather than at any pretrial proceeding. Defendant also argued that the prosecutor abused her discretion when she sought the death penalty against him. The court also rejected this argument finding that there was no evidence that the prosecutor sought the death penalty against defendant in an irrational, inconsistent or discriminatory manner. Further, defendant failed to prove his claim that it was a mandatory policy in the county where he was convicted to impose the death penalty for all capital cases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for the crimes of murder and robbery in the first degree.

 

1066 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Chesapeake Outdoor Enterprises, Inc. v. Baltimore


No. 1721, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


89 Md. App. 54; 597 A.2d 503; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 207



October 30, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City; Joseph H.H. Kaplan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, advertisers, challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) which granted the motions of appellees, Mayor and City Council of Baltimore, for dismissal and summary judgment. The advertisers contended that a previous settlement agreement was enforceable, that Md. Code Ann. art. 25, § 122E applied to appellees, that the trial court's order violated Md. R. BB78, and that summary judgment was improper.


OVERVIEW: The City of Baltimore sought an injunction for removal of the advertisers' signs as violating the Baltimore Zoning Ordinance, despite a settlement agreement reached with the Mayor. The advertisers filed a suit challenging the injunction as a breach of contract and a violation of their constitutional and statutory rights. The court entered summary judgment for the appellees and ordered removal of the signs. On appeal, the court affirmed he judgment and order. The court held that the settlement agreement was void because it purported to bargain away the city's ability to enforce its zoning ordinance. The court held that although Md. Code Ann. art. 25, § 122E did apply to the appellees because it was intended to apply to Baltimore City, the error did not prejudice the advertisers because they failed to present any evidence that its signs were lawfully erected. The appellees' action could not represent an unconstitutional or illegal taking because the advertisers failed to show any evidence that the signs were lawfully erected or maintained. Finally, the trial court's order did not violate Md. R. BB78(a) because it gave the advertisers a fair guide as to their responsibilities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the advertiser's claims of breach of contract, its constitutional and statutory claims of violation of its right to just compensation for deprivation of its property, the summary dismissal of the case, and the order. The court further held that although the trial court improperly held the statute inapplicable, the error did not warrant reversal because it did not prejudice the advertisers.

 

1067 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Shanty Town Assoc. Ltd. Partnership v. Department of Environment


No. 1139, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


89 Md. App. 1; 596 A.2d 1079; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 199



October 15, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Worcester County; Theodore R. Eschenburg, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developer challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Worcester County (Maryland), which affirmed the denial by appellee, Maryland Department of the Environment (MDE), of the developer's application for increased sewer service to support the proposed expansion of certain commercial facilities.


OVERVIEW: The local sanitary commission had entered into an agreement with the Environmental Protection Agency (EPA), pursuant to which the EPA offered certain assistance in improving the sewer system in exchange for an agreement limiting future development. When the developer sought to further develop an existing property, the Maryland Department of the Environment (MDE) held that the agreement with the EPA precluded expansion of sewer service to the property. The trial court agreed, but on appeal, the court reversed. The court first held that the provision of the agreement upon which the trial court relied did not apply because it only identified the geographical area the new system would serve. The court noted that the applicable paragraph prohibited sewer service to undeveloped lots not previously platted. Because the subject property had been previously platted as a single lot, it was not barred from expanded service. However, the agreement did not permit unlimited service, but limited expanded service to one equivalent dwelling unit per lot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court, which held that the consent order barred any expansion of sewer service to development, and remanded to the Secretary of the MDE for further proceedings consistent with the order.

Alexander & Alexander v. B. Dixon Evander & Assocs.


No. 1920, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


88 Md. App. 672; 596 A.2d 687; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 196



October 4, 1991  
October 4, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two Appeals From the Circuit Court for Baltimore City; Meyer M. Cardin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: PUNITIVE DAMAGE AWARD AGAINST APPELLANT SHAND VACATED; PUNITIVE DAMAGE AWARD AGAINST APPELLANT A & A VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY FOR NEW TRIAL AS TO PUNITIVE DAMAGES AGAINST A & A, IN ACCORDANCE WITH THIS OPINION; JUDGMENTS OTHERWISE AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID ONE-THIRD BY APPELLEE, ONE-THIRD BY APPELLANTS SHAND AND MUTUAL FIRE, AND ONE-THIRD BY APPELLANTS A & A AND SCHEELER.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, hospitals and their new insurer, appealed from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which awarded plaintiff insurer $ 12.5 million in punitive damages, based on a jury verdict in an action for tortious interference with a contract, breach of contract, and civil conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff insurer brought an action against defendants, hospitals and their new insurer, as a result of defendant hospitals' decision to terminate their relationship with plaintiff, alleging tortious interference with a contract, breach of contract, and civil conspiracy. The jury returned verdicts for plaintiff and awarded $ 12.5 million in punitive damages. Defendants appealed from the decision. The court accepted the lower court's conclusions that defendants set out to cause economic harm to a competitor, that it used inappropriate means to achieve that goal, and that it should be punished for, and others should be deterred from, engaging in that conduct. Thus, the court vacated the award and directed a new trial on the issue of whether defendants conduct justified an award of punitive damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment for plaintiff insurer against defendants, hospitals and their new insurer, in an action for tortious interference with a contract, breach of contract, and civil conspiracy. However, the court vacated the punitive damages award for $ 12.5 million as excessive and ordered a new trial on that issue.

 

1069 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Wheeler v. State


No. 1641, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


88 Md. App. 512; 596 A.2d 78; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 189



October 1, 1991  
October 1, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Allegany County; J. Frederick Sharer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Allegany County (Maryland). A jury convicted defendant of first degree rape, second degree rape, first degree sexual offense, second degree sexual offense, kidnapping, and assault with intent to rape. The trial court merged the convictions for second degree rape, sexual offense, and assault and sentenced defendant to life terms for rape and sexual offense and 30 years for kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: A complaining witness testified that defendant lured her away, produced a gun and told her he had a knife, and forced her to engage in sexual acts. The trial court convicted defendant of rape, sexual offense, and kidnapping. The court affirmed. Defendant's right to a speedy trial was not violated notwithstanding the 22-month delay in bringing defendant to trial. None of the delay was attributable solely to the state. The lengthy delay occasioned by the pregnancy complications of the complaining witness was a neutral period not chargeable to either party. The remaining delays were caused either by defendant or jointly by defendant and the state. Defendant also failed to assert his speedy trial right until just before the trial. The trial court did not err in allowing the complaining witness to remain in the courtroom after she testified in the state's case-in-chief and to testify as a rebuttal witness. Pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 620, the trial court had to allow a victim of a crime of violence to remain in the courtroom after testifying even if a sequestration order was in effect; the victim could only be excluded for the same reasons that defendant could be excluded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for rape, sexual offense, and kidnapping.

Berry v. Department of Human Resources


No. 1666, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


88 Md. App. 461; 594 A.2d 1258; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 177



September 10, 1991  
September 10, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City; Ellen M. Heller, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANTS TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employees brought a class action against defendants, state agencies and officials and challenged defendants' method of promoting certain individuals as violating the employees' civil rights. The Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) granted defendants' motion to dismiss certain claims, struck the employees' amended complaint as untimely, and disposed of the remaining claims by summary judgment. The employees appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employees claimed that defendants denied their civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, discriminated against them based on race, and violated the state merit system law. The claims were based on allegations that defendants used various procedures to promote "preferred and pre-selected" individuals to vacant or newly created positions, denying plaintiff employees the opportunity to apply for and obtain the positions. The court affirmed and found that the trial court properly struck the amended complaint to prevent the injustice that would result from the delay. As to the § 1983 claim, the court found that the employees failed to clearly allege that they were actually eligible for the positions and that the techniques used were impermissible. Further, the techniques used were part of the merit system and any property interest that the employees had was in the application of the merit system as a whole. As to the individual claims, the court found that the filing of a federal action and voluntary dismissal did not toll a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1981 claim. Another individual failed to show that there was a vacancy and that she was improperly denied a promotion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the employees' action and the striking of the amended complaint.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant construction company sought review of the order of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which dismissed its action to invoke the Mechanics' Lien Statute, Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 9-101 to 9-204 (1981), against appellee church.

On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the matter for further proceedings. The court found that there was no evidence of a legislative intent to preclude a subcontractor from acquiring a mechanics' lien when an owner decided to be its own general contractor. The court determined that the same entity could function as both owner and contractor in mechanics' lien cases.

Miles v. State


No. 1660, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


88 Md. App. 360; 594 A.2d 1208; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 183



September 6, 1991  
September 6, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied December 20, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Jacob S. Levin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of first degree murder and other charges related to the shooting death of the victim in the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland). Defendant appealed, raising issues related to his arrest, trial conduct, and his status as a minor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the judge should have recused himself, a juror should have been disqualified, conduct of voir dire was improper, his arrest was illegal, state's opening statement was improper, and he should have been granted reverse waiver. The court held that the judge's decision to revoke bond, which was reversed on appeal, and pretrial publicity did not require recusal because there were no allegations of personal misconduct by the judge. And, it was not necessary to disqualify a juror who knew a police officer witness because the trial court was diligent in determining whether the juror prejudiced defendant, and defendant failed to show that the juror denied him a fair trial. Defendant's proposed questions were covered by the trial court's voir dire that inquired into the effect of the pretrial publicity. The witness who provided the information in support of defendant's arrest was not anonymous and provided verifiable information to establish probable cause for defendant's arrest. Defendant did not establish that state's opening statement was in bad faith, and Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 594A(b)(3) prohibiting reverse waiver did not deprive defendant of due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder and related offenses.

 

1073 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Harmony v. State


No. 1617, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


88 Md. App. 306; 594 A.2d 1182; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 178



September 5, 1991  
September 5, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County; James T. Smith, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) of third degree sexual offense, fourth degree sexual offense, and battery of a minor child. Prior to trial, defendant moved to dismiss the criminal information because of its alleged vagueness and uncertainty as to time. The trial court denied the motion to dismiss. Defendant appealed his conviction and the denial of his motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of ongoing sexual abuse. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in refusing to dismiss the criminal information because of vagueness and uncertainty; refusing to dismiss the misdemeanor counts which were barred by the statute of limitations, permitting hearsay testimony concerning statements the victim made to a relative several hours after the incident, and refusing to permit the defense to explore issues of potential bias of the victim toward defendant. The court affirmed. The information and bill of particulars stated the times of the offences with reasonable particularity. Where the exact time and date of the crime alleged was impossible to establish, a criminal defendant would not be allowed to "thwart justice" by demanding specific dates and times by raising an alibi defense. Statute of limitations defense was not presented at trial, thus the issue could not be considered on appeal. The prosecution properly laid the foundation for a hearsay exception regarding victim's excited utterance and was properly admitted as such or as a timely complaint of sexual offense. The trial court properly disallowed testimony that would attack victim's character.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for sexual offense and battery of a minor child.

Reynolds v. State


No. 1247, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


88 Md. App. 197; 594 A.2d 609; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 162



August 29, 1991  
August 29, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Carroll County; Donald J. Gilmore, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction by a jury in the Circuit Court for Carroll County (Maryland), of second-degree rape, a second-degree sexual offense, assault with intent to rape, assault with intent to commit a second-degree sexual offense, and incest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant gave statements to a counsellor, after he signed a consent form that required notification of the police of revealed child abuse. As a result of his statements the police met him at the counsellor's office and at his home, and he made incriminating statements that were used against him in his trial. After his conviction, he appealed and claimed that the trial court had erred when it admitted his various incriminating admissions and confessions that should have been suppressed because they were obtained in violation of the privilege against compelled self-incrimination of the Fifth Amendment and the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment of the Federal Constitution and of their Maryland counterparts, Articles 22 and 23 of the Maryland Declaration of Rights. The court affirmed the convictions because there was no privilege, statute or rule that protected defendant's statements to the counsellor. Since the counsellor was a private party there was no constitutional issue. The Miranda protection in the Fifth Amendment did not apply because defendant was not in custody when he gave the statements to the police. There was no evidence that the statements were coerced.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed all of defendant's convictions and denied his appeal based on alleged violation of his privilege against compelled self-incrimination of the Fifth Amendment and the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment and their Maryland counterparts.

Kinser v. State


No. 1498, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


88 Md. App. 17; 591 A.2d 894; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 149



June 28, 1991  
June 28, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal From the Circuit Court for Baltimore City, David B. Mitchell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which convicted him on a jury verdict that found defendant guilty of battery, possession of a deadly weapon, and racial assault.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of battery, possession of a deadly weapon, and racial assault. On appeal, defendant claimed that the evidence was insufficient to support the racial assault conviction. The court disagreed, finding that there was direct evidence that defendant's actions were motivated by race. First, a police officer testified that immediately before defendant's arrest he used racial slurs when he told the officer that he'd take care of the minority. Secondly, defendant's motive was inferred not just from his words but also from acts and conduct, and defendant's conduct overwhelmingly demonstrated that his actions were motivated by racial animus. Evidence of a lynch mob was not offered to charge defendant with responsibility for the crowd's actions and words, but to show his own state of mind because for a considerable period of time he was in the crowd, not as an observer, but as an active participant. There was no merit to defendant's claim that he did nothing that indicated that his actions were motivated by race. Rather, there was clearly sufficient evidence to support the racial assault conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

 

1076 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Spates v. Montgomery County


No. 1440 September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


87 Md. App. 590; 590 A.2d 1074; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 138



June 4, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; J. James McKenna, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER DISMISSING SECOND AMENDED COMPLAINT VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY FOR ENTRY OF DECLARATORY JUDGMENT IN CONFORMANCE WITH THIS OPINION; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which granted the motion to dismiss filed by appellees, a county and the State of Maryland. The taxpayer had requested a declaratory judgment that the imposition of state and county taxes on landowners was unconstitutional because personal property such as mortgages, stocks, and bonds were not taxed, which placed an unfair burden on landowners.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer claimed that the scheme of taxing real property but not personal property offended Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 15 and the federal Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses. Appellees' motion to dismiss argued that the taxpayer failed to allege any special damage or special interest that was distinct from that of the general public, did not present an "actual controversy," and by omitting to specify the particular statutes challenged, failed to present a justiciable controversy. The court held that: (1) although the trial court never signed an order granting the motion to dismiss, the record as a whole showed than an appealable order had been issued; (2) because the taxpayer challenged the system of taxation, it was not necessary for him to specify the particular sections of the law that offended him; (3) the taxpayer did not explain how the state's system of taxation harmed him; and (4) the legislature's refusal to tax all real and personal property in the state did not render the property tax violative of Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 15 or the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order dismissing the taxpayer's complaint and remanded the matter for entry of a declaratory judgment.

General Motors Corp. v. Public Service Com.


No. 1080, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


87 Md. App. 321; 589 A.2d 982; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 118



May 13, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Three Appeals from the Circuit Court for Hartford County; Brodnax Cameron, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANTS TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, corporation and others, sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Hartford County (Maryland), which affirmed two orders of appellee Maryland Public Service Commission. Appellants argued that appellee's conclusion that it was federally preempted from requiring local distribution companies to absorb any part of the take or pay cost provisions, other than for imprudence, was in error.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court affirmed appellee Maryland Public Service Commission's (PSC) order, which held that appellants, corporation and others, were federally preempted from requiring local distribution company's from absorbing any part of take or pay provisions, other than for imprudence, appellants sought review. Appellants argued that appellee PSC erred in allowing the pass-through in the form of the purchased gas allowance rather than in the context of a rate hearing at which evidence could be presented. Appellee gas companies responded by noting that a number of semi-annual reviews had already occurred and requested either that the appeal be dismissed as premature or that appellee PSC records in those proceedings be added to the appellate record. The court affirmed, holding that in reviewing the local distribution company's procurement practices, appellee PSC reasonably concluded that take or pay costs were necessary and proper expenses that should be allowed under Md. Ann. Code art. 78, § 69 and were costs of purchased gas that should be recoverable under Md. Ann. Code art. 78, §§54 and 54D.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of appellee Maryland Public Service Commission (PSC), which concluded that take or pay costs were properly treated as costs of purchased gas. The court held that the conclusion was neither illegal, arbitrary, nor unreasonable and that subject to a review of the local distribution company's procurement practices, appellee PSC reasonably concluded that these costs were necessary and proper expenses of purchased gas.

Durham v. Fields


No. 959, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


87 Md. App. 1; 588 A.2d 352; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 92



April 5, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied August 15, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City; Hilary D. Caplan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT ENTERED ON COUNT I, INCLUDING JUDGMENT FOR PUNITIVE DAMAGES, REVERSED; JUDGMENT ENTERED ON COUNT II AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID ONE-HALF BY APPELLANTS, ONE-HALF BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employee, a college administrator, filed a wrongful discharge case against defendant employer in the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which awarded judgment to the employee. The employee previously lost a federal case that was arguably grounded on the same facts. The employer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee had worked first as a college faculty member and then as a member of the administration of the same institution; the employee had been dismissed from the administrative position. The employer averred that the federal case was res judicata, that there was no due process violation, that the employee had lost or waived faculty tenure status when the employee became an administrator, and that the evidence was legally insufficient to support an award of punitive damages. The court held that (1) the federal decisions were not res judicata largely because the federal court declined to exercise its pendent jurisdiction over all state claims; (2) the failure of the employer to scrupulously follow the procedures for evaluating the employee's performance did not reach constitutional proportions; (3) the employer failed to show that the employee's faculty tenure rights had been lost or waived; and (4) the punitive damages had been submitted solely with respect to the due process claim, which was unsupported.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment entered on the employee's due process claim and the punitive damage award. The court affirmed the judgment on the employee's breach of contract claim.

Weathersby v. Kentucky Fried Chicken Nat'l Management Co.

86 Md. App. 533; 587 A.2d 569; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 79

1080 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Ocean City v. Purnell-Jarvis, Ltd.


No. 802, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


86 Md. App. 390; 586 A.2d 816; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 70



March 6, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two Appeals from the Circuit Court for Worcester County; Thomas C. Groton, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART. CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR WORCESTER COUNTY WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REMAND TO THE MARYLAND TAX COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS IN ACCORDANCE WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID THREE-FOURTHS BY OCEAN CITY AND ONE-FOURTH BY PURNELL-JARVIS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The circuit court for Worcester County (Maryland) reversed a judgment of a lower court and remanded plaintiff corporation's refund matter. Defendant city and the corporation both appealed. The lower court had ruled that the corporation was entitled to a refund for 1984, but not for 1983 and six percent per annum interest from the date of payment of each fee subject to a refund. The corporation had paid fees related to construction.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court found that the corporation had, in fact, paid the fees which it alleged were illegally assessed. The court held that the corporation had standing to seek the refund of the fees it paid in conjunction with both lump-sum and cost-plus contracts. Because it was clear that the fee schedules at issue were in the nature of regulatory measures, the amount of money that the city officials had intended to raise, as opposed to what those measures actually raised, was not the test that should have been be applied in determining reasonableness. Therefore, the court held that the trial court erred when it considered the intent of the city officials in determining whether the 1983 fee schedule was reasonable. The court held that the interest on any refund allowed in the case was to be paid at the old rate of six percent from the date the taxes were paid until July 1, 1987. After that date, interest was to accrue at the new variable rate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded the matter. The court held that the corporation had standing to seek the refund, that the trial court erroneously considered the city's intent in determining the validity of the fee schedule, and that the circuit court properly remanded the case for to the trial court for a determination of the reasonableness of the fee schedules.

Md. Comm'n on Human Rels. v. Mayor & Balt.


No. 395, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


86 Md. App. 167; 586 A.2d 37; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 50; 3 Am. Disabilities Cas. (BNA) 1291



February 27, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City; Thomas Ward, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The former employee filed a complaint with appellant, the Maryland Commission on Human Relations (commission), alleging discriminatory termination in her employment. The hearing examiner found in favor the former employee and against appellees, mayor and city. The commission appeal board affirmed the hearing examiner's decision, and the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) reversed. The commission sought review.


OVERVIEW: The former employee was terminated from her employment as a police officer for the city because she was emotionally incapacitated. Thereafter, she filed a complaint with the commission alleging discrimination. After administrative hearings, the lower court reversed the commission appeal board's finding in favor of the former employee. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the holding of the hearing examiner, adopted by the commission appeal board, clearly set forth that the former employee, at the time of her discharge, was not qualified to perform the duties and essential functions of a police officer. The court held that the case should have been concluded because, even with accommodation, the former employee was incapable of performing the essential functions of a police officer. The court held that Md. Ann. Code art. 49 prohibited discharge only if a reasonable accommodation would have enabled the handicapped person to perform the essential functions of the position the person involved was hired to perform. The court held that the lower court did not substitute its judgment for that of the commission and his decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which reversed the decision of the commission appeal board, in the former employee's action for alleged discriminatory termination of her employment. The court ordered costs to be paid by the commission.

 

1082 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


State Rds. Com. of State Highway Admin. v. G. L. Cornell Co. Sav. & Profit Sharing Trust


No. 502, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


85 Md. App. 765; 584 A.2d 1331; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 30



February 1, 1991  
February 1, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 11, 1991.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT FOR PRE-JUDGMENT INTEREST VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS IN ACCORDANCE WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE DIVIDED EQUALLY BETWEEN THE PARTIES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State Roads Commission, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which awarded appellee landowner prejudgment interest at nine percent in a "quick take" condemnation action.


OVERVIEW: The owner sought pre-judgment interest in a "quick take" condemnation action by the Commission. In such a case because the owner did not receive the full fair value of his property until sometime after the taking, the payment of pre-judgment interest on the difference between what he received and what he was entitled to was designed to pay the owner for the "time value" of the money he should have received on the day the land was taken. The court concluded that in a "quick take" action the owner was entitled to pre-judgment interest. In this case, the owner rejected a just compensation analysis in favor of Md. Code Ann., transp. § 8-330. Having chosen that course, the court held that, the owner must be content with the benefits (and limitations) afforded by the statute. Accordingly, the court concluded that where, as here, the owner insisted upon the alternate valuation date under § 8-330, he was entitled to such pre-judgment interest as may be afforded under Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 8-331, at the six percent rate, and not to anything more. The court vacated the award of pre-judgment interest and remanded for an appropriate recalculation of that interest.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment and remanded for further proceedings in accordance with the court's decision.

State v. Ott


No. 1218, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


85 Md. App. 632; 584 A.2d 1266; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 25



January 29, 1991  
January 29, 1991, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] ORDER GRANTING MOTION TO SUPPRESS REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FREDERICK COUNTY FOR TRIAL; APPELLEE TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Frederick County (Maryland), which granted defendant's motion to suppress after he was charged with possession of a controlled dangerous substance, possession of a controlled dangerous substance with intent to distribute, and possession of drug paraphernalia.


OVERVIEW: In a deserted lot where the officer knew thefts and acts of vandalism had previously occurred, he observed a sole parked vehicle. He requested identification from defendant and the other occupant of the vehicle. When he ran a computer check, he learned that an outstanding warrant existed for defendant. The officer arrested defendant and, after searching the vehicle, found cocaine. Later that day, the officer learned that in fact the outstanding warrant had been served before defendant's arrest but was not removed from the computer until after the arrest. Defendant filed a motion to suppress. The trial court granted the motion. On appeal, the court reversed, finding that the officer's request for defendant's identification was not a seizure under the Fourth Amendment. The good faith exception to the exclusionary rule applied to justify the warrantless arrest because the warrant only remained in the computer four days longer than it should have. The warrantless search of the vehicle was valid as a search incident to a lawful arrest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which had granted defendant's motion to suppress, and remanded the case to the trial court for trial.

Lone v. Montgomery County

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owners of nonconforming multi-family housing challenged decisions of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which entered judgments for appellee county in its actions for injunctions against appellants' multi-family use of property after the ten-year amortization period for changing nonconforming multi-family housing to single-family use.
