The judgments were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments for appellee county in its actions for injunctions against appellant owners of nonconforming multi-family housing, holding that the ten-year amortization period for changing nonconforming multi-family housing to single-family use was constitutional.

 

1085 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


M & G Convoy, Inc. v. Mauk


No. 279, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


85 Md. App. 394; 584 A.2d 101; 1991 Md. App. LEXIS 15



January 17, 1991  
January 17, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 11, 1991.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer and insurer sought review of the judgment of the Maryland Workers' Compensation Commission that had rendered a decision in favor of appellee employee. The Circuit Court for Cecil County remanded the case and found that under the circumstances, the mere receipt of benefits under the workers' compensation laws of another state did not bar the claim for such benefits in Maryland. Appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: The employer sought review of the Maryland Workers' Compensation Commission (commission) decision. The employee had sustained injuries while attempting to chain automobiles onto a trailer. The employer contended that the trial court erred in failing to find the employee's election of a Pennsylvania remedy barred recovery under the Maryland Workers' Compensation Act as a matter of law and in remanding the case to the commission without deciding all outstanding issues on appeal in the trial court. The employer contended that the employee had made a binding election to proceed in Pennsylvania, and, therefore, should be precluded from proceeding in Maryland as a matter of public policy. The court disagreed with this contention. The employer argued that Pennsylvania law precluded recovery of permanent partial benefits because the employee's injury fell under "other cases." The court did not find this argument persuasive because it did not rise to the level necessary to overcome the avowed remedial purpose of workers' compensation laws.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court rendered in favor of employee and which held that the mere receipt of benefits under the workers' compensation law of another state did not bar the claim for such benefits in Maryland.

 

1086 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Supervisor of Assessments v. Scheidt


No. 178, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


85 Md. App. 154; 582 A.2d 563; 1990 Md. App. LEXIS 195



November 30, 1990  
November 30, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied March 22, 1991.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HOWARD COUNTY VACATED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO ENTER A JUDGMENT AFFIRMING THE JUDGMENT OF THE MARYLAND TAX COURT. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Supervisor of Assessments of Howard County sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Howard County (Maryland), which overturned a tax court's decision sustaining a decision of the Supervisor denying appellee residuary trustees' request for a refund of an Agricultural Land Transfer Tax (ALTT) and remanded the case to the tax court for a further remand to the Supervisor for a recalculation of the ALTT.


OVERVIEW: Appellees transferred land. The transfer triggered the ALTT because approximately three-quarters of an acre was assessed as agricultural. Appellees argued that the formula mandated by the ALTT, as applied to them, denied them due process of law. Appellees also argued that the formula for determining the amount of consideration allocable to the agricultural land violated the Equal Protection Clause because the application of the formula to mixed residential and agricultural land transfers created a classification that was hostile and oppressive to landowners whose residential property was underassessed. The court found that the formula was not haphazard, arbitrary, or capricious and thus did not deny due process of law. Appellees, after they received the estimated ALTT, asked for and received a reassessment of their residential property. If that reassessment grossly undervalued their property, appellees could have appealed, but they chose not to do so. The statutorily mandated formula for computing the amount of consideration allocable to the agricultural land transferred in a mixed residential-agricultural land transaction did not violate equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the circuit court's judgment.

 

1087 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Meyer v. State Farm Fire & Casualty Co.


No. 981, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


85 Md. App. 83; 582 A.2d 275; 1990 Md. App. LEXIS 182



November 28, 1990  
November 28, 1990, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANTS TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant policy holders sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Wicomico County (Maryland), which dismissed the policy holders' suit for damages against appellee insurance carrier for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The policy holders argued that the trial court's enforcement of an appraisal provision, after being invoked by the insurance carrier, violated their constitutional right to a trial by jury.


OVERVIEW: Policy holders had purchased a fire insurance policy from an insurance carrier. After a fire occurred at the policy holders' home, and the policy holders and the insurance carrier could not agree on the amount of loss, the insurance carrier invoked the policy's appraisal provision. The policy holders countered by filing a suit for damages against the insurance carrier. On a motion by the insurance carrier, the trial court dismissed the policy holders' suit for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. On appeal, the court affirmed. Specifically, the court held that although all insurance policies are contracts of adhesion, that fact alone does not make an appraisal provision unconscionable. Moreover, the court ruled that judicial enforcement of an appraisal provision that makes an appraisal, if invoked by the insurer, a condition precedent to a suit by the policy holders, is not an unconstitutional deprivation of the right to trial by jury. Accordingly, the court concluded that the appraisal provision in this case was not invalid, and that the procedure required by it must be used in good faith.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the policy holders' suit for damages against the insurance carrier. In particular, the court held that judicial enforcement of an otherwise valid appraisal provision in an insurance policy does not deprive the policy holders of their constitutional right to a trial by jury, and that there was no basis for determining that the appraisal provision in this case was invalid.

Hickory Hills Ltd. Partnership v. Secretary of State


No. 51, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


84 Md. App. 677; 581 A.2d 834; 1990 Md. App. LEXIS 173



November 7, 1990  
November 7, 1990, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] APPELLEE'S MOTION TO DISMISS GRANTED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee secretary filed a motion to dismiss the review filed by appellant corporation from an order of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which remanded the case involving an express warranty to the secretary for the taking of additional evidence.


OVERVIEW: The secretary had made a preliminary determination that the corporation had not complied with its promise contained in the public offering statement to spend at least a certain amount on road improvements. The secretary had determined that the corporation did spend the money on paving but that the condominium association reimbursed it for that amount and, therefore, the corporation had violated its express warranty to spend its own money on paving. The issue was whether an order of the circuit court, remanding to the secretary for taking of additional evidence when the circuit court had not yet heard or decided the appeal, was a final order, and therefore, appealable. The court granted the secretary's motion to dismiss the appeal. The court found that, under Md. Code Ann. State Gov't § 10-215(e), the circuit court had continuing jurisdiction over the appeal from the administrative agency, had to review the additional evidence taken by agency, and complete its appellate hearing on the merits. The court concluded, therefore, that such a remand was not a final, appealable order.


OUTCOME: The secretary's motion to dismiss the appeal by the corporation from an order remanding the express warranty case to the secretary was granted.

 

1089 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Clearail, Inc. v. Mardirossian Family Enterprises


No. 808, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


84 Md. App. 497; 581 A.2d 36; 1990 Md. App. LEXIS 158



October 30, 1990  
October 30, 1990, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT REVERSED; CASE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS IN ACCORDANCE WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE PAID ONE-HALF BY APPELLANT AND ONE-HALF BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant subcontractor challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which dismissed its action to establish and enforce a mechanics' lien against appellee partnership on the ground that the subcontractor had not complied with the notice requirements of Md. Code Ann. Real Property § 9-104.


OVERVIEW: The subcontractor sent two separate notices to the partnership of its intention to a claim mechanics' lien. Both notices were sent within the 90-day statutory period in Md. Code Ann. Real Property § 9-104. They were sent by certified mail and were returned unopened. After expiration of the 90 days, the subcontractor arranged for personal service of the notice, which was successful. The lower court dismissed the subcontractor's action to enforce the lien for failure to comply with § 9-104. The court reversed. The court held that the mechanics' lien had to be sent within the statutory period and received within a reasonable time thereafter. It was not clear whether the partnership attempted to avoid service. The court remanded for a determination of whether the partnership acted in good faith vis-a-vis the certified mail; whether any payments were made during the interim between the 90th day and the receipt of actual notice; and what actions the subcontractor took to effect delivery.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's dismissal of the subcontractor's action to enforce its mechanics' lien against the partnership and remanded for factual findings as to whether there was substantial compliance with the statutory requirements for enforcement of mechanics' liens.

 

1090 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thornton


Misc. No. 51, September Term, 1990


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


84 Md. App. 312; 578 A.2d 1212; 1990 Md. App. LEXIS 149



September 7, 1990  
September 7, 1990, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] APPLICATION DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed an application for leave to appeal an order of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which reduced the amount and conditions of defendant's bail while he was awaiting trial on criminal charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by indictment with various offenses under the controlled dangerous substance laws. At a hearing, the trial court entered an order setting cash bail. Defendant filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, seeking relief from that order. The hearing judge found that bail was excessive and issued the writ, releasing defendant upon posting a reduced bail on a corporate bond only. The State sought review. The court denied the application. An appeal could only be taken of a final order in a habeas corpus case where it was specifically authorized by statute. Under Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-707, defendant was the only person who could appeal from an order denying bail or setting excessive bail. There was no statutory authority for the State to seek appellate review. The broad language of the Post Conviction Procedures Act did not authorize appellate review of a habeas corpus order, especially because appellate review was dealt with specifically in Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-706. The court concluded that no statutory authority existed for the seeking of appellate review by the State from a writ of habeas corpus issued pursuant to § 3-706.


OUTCOME: The court denied the State's application.

St. George Antiochian Orthodox Christian Church v. Aggarwal


No. 1638, September Term, 1989


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


83 Md. App. 599; 576 A.2d 224; 1990 Md. App. LEXIS 132



July 13, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal From the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Joseph S. Casula, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant church sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which ruled in favor of appellee property purchasers who obtained an order foreclosing the church's right to redeem the property.


OVERVIEW: The church received a parcel of land as a donation. The church believed that it had tax exempt status with regard to the land and had no knowledge of the taxes charged on the property. The property purchaser bought the land at a tax sale and obtained an order foreclosing the church's right to redeem the property. On appeal, the church claimed that it never received actual notice of the sale or of the foreclosure proceedings. The court held that the provisions of Md. Code Ann. Tax-Prop. § 14-833 et seq., as they related to proceedings for the foreclosure of the rights of redemption, were constitutional. The court held that the notice provisions were constitutional whether actual service was made, so long as substantial adherence to the statute's requirements were met. The court held that the alleged deficiencies in notice did not cause the proceeding to be jurisdictionally deficient nor did they constitute actual fraud.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the property purchaser in his claim to obtain an order foreclosing the church's right to redeem the property.

Cade v. Montgomery County


No. 1161, September Term, 1989


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


83 Md. App. 419; 575 A.2d 744; 1990 Md. App. LEXIS 115



June 27, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied August 30, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Appeals from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; William M. Cave, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant towing companies sought a declaration that appellee county's ordinance regulating the towing of motor vehicles from private property without the vehicle owners' consent was unconstitutional. The parties each appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) which declared the ordinance unconstitutional as in excess of the county's police power.


OVERVIEW: The county's ordinance, Montgomery County, Md., County Council Bill No. 16-87, required private property owners to post signs notifying the public of any parking restrictions, limited the distance cars improperly parked on private property could be towed, required towing companies to accept major credit cards or personal checks for towed vehicles, and imposed other towing restrictions. On appeal, the court noted that an ordinance, like a statute, is presumptively valid. The court found that no evidence existed on the record to support the trial court's finding that the ordinance interfered with the rights of private property owners and was unduly restrictive upon them. Further, the court found that the ordinance was a proper exercise of the county's police power, as it bore a reasonable and substantial relation to the safety and welfare of the people and to the goals of the county council. Lastly, the court found that the payment of towing fees by the tender of personal checks or credit cards as mandated by ordinance did not create a new form of legal tender or regulate its value in violation of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment which held that the county's ordinance was an unconstitutional exercise of police power.

 

1093 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Simms v. State


No. 1542, September Term, 1989


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


83 Md. App. 204; 574 A.2d 12; 1990 Md. App. LEXIS 95



May 31, 1990 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of judgments from the Circuit Court for Howard County (Maryland) that entered convictions, after a jury trial, for daytime housebreaking and misdemeanor theft charges. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 643B (b)(1957).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of daytime housebreaking and misdemeanor theft charges after a jury returned guilty verdicts on those charges. He was sentence to life in prison without parole pursuant to § 643B (b). On appeal, he contended that the trial court erred in not dismissing the charges against him because they were not set for trial within 180 days; permitting the state to introduce evidence of other crimes; and by sentencing him to life in prison without parole. The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court. The court held that defendant requested the continuance causing the delay, and he had previously failed to appear on the prior trial date. In addition, his flight upon being discovered at the crime scene was relevant to proving his guilt without simply showing propensity. Moreover, a prior conviction could not be collaterally attacked in a sentencing proceeding in a subsequent case. Defendant was not, as he claimed, being penalized twice for the prior crimes. The state properly used the predicate offenses invoked in the prior proceeding again in the current sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court that convicted defendant of daytime housebreaking and misdemeanor theft charges, and sentenced him to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole as a habitual offender.

Edmonds v. Murphy


No. 1480, September Term, 1989


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


83 Md. App. 133; 573 A.2d 853; 1990 Md. App. LEXIS 93



May 30, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Baltimore County; Joseph F. Murphy, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART; 1/2 COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS; 1/2 COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tortfeasor and his employer filed a motion to apply Md. Cts. & Jud. Proc. Code Ann. § 11-108(b) to the non-economic damages awarded to appellee claimant and her husband and a motion for remittitur, or, in the alternative, for a new trial, pursuant to Md. R. Civ. P. 2-533. The Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) denied the motions and entered judgment for the claimant and her husband. The tortfeasor and employer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was injured when the tire of the truck, driven by the tortfeasor and owned by his employer, exploded causing the truck to collide with the claimant's car. In their personal injury suit, the claimant and her husband alleged that the tire had not been inspected properly and that the tortfeasor's act of diving to the truck's floor at the time of the accident constituted gross negligence. The jury awarded compensatory and punitive damages. The trial court refused to apply the statutory damages cap. The tortfeasor and the employer appealed. On appeal, the court held that the cap, set forth in Md. Cts. & Jud. Proc. Code Ann. § 11-108(b), applied and did not violate due process, the separation of powers doctrine, or equal protection principles; that the damages awarded for the pecuniary components of the loss of consortium claim were not subject to the cap; that punitive damages should not have been awarded because the evidence did not establish gross negligence; that sufficient evidence justified the award of compensatory damages based on the negligent failure to inspect the tire; and that the challenges to the jury instructions had not been preserved for review.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the award of punitive damages, reduced the award of compensatory damages, and affirmed the award of damages for household services.

Stach v. Stach


No. 1643, September Term, 1989


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


83 Md. App. 36; 573 A.2d 409; 1990 Md. App. LEXIS 89



May 10, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal From The Circuit Court for Baltimore County, John Grason Turnbull, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: MOTION TO DISMISS AND FOR SANCTIONS DENIED. JUDGMENT REVERSED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of an immediate order entered by the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which incorporated the report of a standing master and granted temporary physical custody of the parties' children to appellee mother and granted the father pendente lite visitation with the children and ordered him to pay for their support. The mother brought a motion to dismiss the appeal and for sanctions.


OVERVIEW: The trial court referred the parties' divorce to a standing master for a report and recommendation concerning pendente lite custody, child support, and visitation. The father filed exceptions to the master's report. The court incorporated the report of the master and issued an immediate order granting temporary physical custody of the children to the mother. The court denied the mother's motion to dismiss the appeal and reversed the order of the trial court. The court held that when a notice of exceptions had been timely filed, the trial court could not enter an immediate order implementing the recommendation by the master that pendente lite custody of children be awarded to the adverse party. The legislative history surrounding the adoption of the predecessor to Md. R. 2-541(g)(2) revealed that the authority of the circuit court to enter such an order was included in an earlier draft of the Rule, but was deleted prior to its adoption. That legislative history was persuasive evidence that the court of appeals did not intend to grant a circuit court such authority.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss and reversed the order of the trial court.

In re Criminal Investigation No. 13


No. 1150, September Term, 1989


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


82 Md. App. 609; 573 A.2d 51; 1990 Md. App. LEXIS 69

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant chemical company challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Dorchester County (Maryland), which denied its request for an ex parte injunction to prevent appellee state's interviewing of the chemical company's employees without corporate counsel's presence.


OVERVIEW: The state began an investigation of the chemical company for alleged violations of Maryland's Hazardous Substance Control Law and Maryland's Water Pollution Control Law. Harris v. State


No. 1212, September Term, 1989


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


82 Md. App. 450; 572 A.2d 573; 1990 Md. App. LEXIS 63



May 1, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Kent County, Elroy G. Boyer, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Kent County (Maryland) that convicted him of both the distribution of cocaine and conspiracy to distribute cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant raised numerous arguments including that because the conspiracy charge against his co-conspirator was nolle prossed, the evidence was not legally sufficient to sustain his conviction for conspiracy. The court affirmed the conviction. Appellant reasoned that the nolle pros amounted to a judicial determination that the co-conspirator did not possess a conspiratorial mens rea and could not, therefore, have been the indispensable second party for the "meeting of criminal minds." The court explained that the cases were divided on this issue and appellant's reasoning encompassed one view. The court, however, chose to adopt the "better reasoned view" and held that the nolle pros of the conspiracy charge against appellant's co-conspirator, entered pursuant to a plea bargain, did not preclude the conspiracy conviction of appellant. The court found that the nolle pros was not a judicial determination that the co-conspirator was, on the merits of his case, not guilty of conspiracy, but merely a declaration that the state would not puruse the charges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Comptroller of Treasury v. Armco Export Sales Corp.


No. 1145, September Term, 1989


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


82 Md. App. 429; 572 A.2d 562; 1990 Md. App. LEXIS 64



May 1, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected May 8, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore City, Meyer N. Cardin, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED. REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Comptroller of the Treasury (comptroller) made corporate income tax assessments against appellee domestic international sales corporations (DISCs) for the years 1981-85. The tax court reversed the assessments against the DISCs reasoning that the comptroller had failed to establish any nexus between Maryland and the DISCs. The Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) affirmed the tax court's decision. The comptroller appealed.


OVERVIEW: The three corporations composing the DISCs were wholly owned subsidiaries of a multinational parent doing business in Maryland and filing a Maryland corporate tax return. Each parent produced goods in Maryland that were exported outside the United States. None of the DISCs had ever filed a Maryland corporation income tax return. The comptroller argued taxation was required by state law and was necessary to reflect the economic reality of the DISCs' transactions. The comptroller argued the DISCs were doing business in Maryland within the meaning of Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 316, and the nexus was established by the parent of the phantom corporation engaged in the export business in the state. The court held that Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 280A(c)(7) expressed a legislative intent to tax income received by a DISC. The three key elements necessary for constitutional nexus were affirmatively established in each of the three DISC cases: the parent was engaged in business in Maryland, the parent was unitary with the DISC, and the apportionment formula was fair. The court held that and under Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 309(c)(2), limitations did not run because the DISCs filed no returns.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's affirmance of the tax court's decision and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

1099 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


County Comm'rs of Carroll County v. Arundel Corp.


No. 1246, September Term, 1989


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


82 Md. App. 418; 571 A.2d 1270; 1990 Md. App. LEXIS 60



April 4, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] TWO APPEALS FROM THE Circuit Court for Carroll County, Donald J. Gimore, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; CASE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS IN ACCORDANCE WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the County Commissioners of Carroll County, Maryland (commissioners), challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Carroll County (Maryland), which reversed a board of zoning appeals' rejection of applications for conditional use permits filed by appellee quarries.


OVERVIEW: After the quarries filed their applications, but prior to action on them, the commissioners revised the county zoning ordinance to require that applications for conditional use permits be accompanied by various documents including a detailed site development plan and a comprehensive hydrogeological study. By its own terms the ordinance became effective immediately. The board than rejected the applications because they failed to comply with the ordinance. On appeal from the board's decision, the trial court held that the ordinance was improperly applied retroactively, and remanded the matter to the board. On appeal, however, the court reversed. The court held that the amendment was procedural because it exclusively addressed the process of applying for the permits and no new standard would be applied by the board when deciding to grant or deny such an application. The ordinance therefore could be applied to pending actions. Retroactive application of the ordinance would not be unfair, and therefore impermissible, because the quarries knew that the ordinance amendment was being considered prior to their submissions of the applications.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had reversed the board's rejection of the applications, and remanded the matter to the trial court with directions to make findings concerning the validity of the ordinance in light of other challenges argued by the quarries.

 

1100 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Passamichali v. State


No. 444, September Term, 1989


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


81 Md. App. 731; 569 A.2d 733; 1990 Md. App. LEXIS 29



February 13, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 22, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore City, Elsbeth L. Bothe, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which entered a jury verdict convicting him of robbery with a dangerous and deadly weapon, transportation of a handgun, and use of a handgun in the commission of a felony or crime of violence.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the per se admissibility of infamous crimes mandated by Md. Code Ann. Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 10-905 (1988) deprived him of his constitutional right to present testimony in his own behalf and to a fair trial, and that defendant's decision to plead not guilty negatively influenced the trial judge resulting in the imposition of a sentence five years in excess of that which had been promised by the court in exchange for a guilty plea. The court affirmed, concluding that: (1) it defied logic to suggest that a defendant had to testify in order to preserve for appellate review a claim of deprivation of the constitutional right to testify; (2) § 10-905(a) was neither an arbitrary nor disproportionate restriction on defendant's right to testify and right to a fair trial and did not conflict with the protections afforded a criminal defendant by the United States Constitution; and (3) the record did not support defendant's contention that the trial court impermissibly considered the fact that defendant refused to plead guilty before imposing a 15 year sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for weapons offenses.

 

1101 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Darrikhuma v. State


No. 672, September Term, 1989


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


81 Md. App. 560; 568 A.2d 1150; 1990 Md. App. LEXIS 18



February 5, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County, H. Chester Goudy, Jr., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) for driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving while intoxicated. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The denial of defendant's motion to dismiss the charging document based on improper service under Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 26-201 (1987 Repl. Vol., 1989 Cum. Supp.), Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc., § 2-605(b) (1984 Repl. Vol.), and Md. R. Crim. Causes 4-212(h) was not error. Although process was legally issued by the arresting officer, the error occurred in its actual service because the District Court Commissioner did not have authority to effectuate service. Because defendant appeared to defend against the charge, the trial court had jurisdiction over the charge and the person. The court found the error in service to be harmless because it in no way influenced the verdict. The trial court did not err by admitting the results of the breathalyzer test because the police did not affirmatively mislead defendant about his right to a preliminary test, but merely properly advised him of his subsequent test rights. The court did not err by limiting defendant's cross-examination of a key state's witness because he was attempting to elicit expert testimony from an unqualified witness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for driving while intoxicated.

 

1102 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Warner v. Ocean City


No. 618, September Term, 1989


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


81 Md. App. 176; 567 A.2d 160; 1989 Md. App. LEXIS 214



December 26, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 16, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Worcester County, Theodore R. Eschenburg, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AS TO THE TRIAL COURT'S RULINGS ON THE CHARGES AFFIRMED; JUDGMENT AS TO THE TRIAL COURT'S AFFIRMANCE OF SANCTIONS REVERSED; ON OUR REMAND THE TRIAL COURT IS TO REMAND TO THE AGENCY WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO THE AGENCY TO RECONSIDER SANCTIONS IN LIGHT OF THE TRIAL COURT'S RULING AND OUR HOLDING; APPELLANT TO PAY 80% OF THE COSTS; APPELLEE TO PAY 20%.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Worcester County (Maryland), which affirmed two of the findings, but reversed the remaining findings, of an administrative hearing board (board) acting under the Law Enforcement Officers Bill of Rights, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 727 et seq. (1957). The trial court affirmed the board's decision recommending the demotion of the police officer from lieutenant to sergeant.


OVERVIEW: The police officer wrote an anonymous letter to the mayor and city council challenging the promotion of a police captain to major. The board, acting pursuant to the Law Enforcement Officers Bill of Rights, rendered a guilty verdict on five charges arising from the communication of the anonymous letter. The trial court affirmed the findings on two of the charges but reversed the remaining findings. The trial court also affirmed the decision of the board to demote the police officer from lieutenant to sergeant. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court because the town's demotion of the police officer was not an unconstitutional interference with the exercise of his First Amendment rights where the letter interfered with the efficient operation of the police department. The court also determined that the trial court made no error in its review of the sufficiency of the evidence. The court, however, reversed the board's decision of demotion and remanded to the board for reconsideration of the demotion in light of the fact that the trial court had reversed three of the board's guilty findings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment upholding two of the board's findings but reversed the trial court's judgment affirming the decision of the board recommending the police officer's demotion from lieutenant to sergeant. The court remanded the matter to the board for a determination as to whether the trial court's reversal of some of the findings merited a different sanction.

Landover Books, Inc. v. Prince George's County


No. 498, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


81 Md. App. 54; 566 A.2d 792; 1989 Md. App. LEXIS 205



December 6, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 6, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Prince George's County, David Gray Ross, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adult bookstore sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which ordered the adult bookstore to cease business operations as a result of its failure to comply with Prince George's County, Md., Code § 27-107.1, et seq.


OVERVIEW: The Prince George's County Council enacted an ordinance, which set forth locational and operational requirements for adult bookstores. Prince George's County, Md., Code § 27-107.1, et seq. The county cited the adult bookstore owner for his failure to comply with the special exception provision of the ordinance. Prince George's County, Md., Code §§ 27-248 and 27-317. The adult bookstore owner initiated an appeal, which was denied by the Board of Zoning Appeals (board) for Prince George's County. The lower court affirmed the board's decision and ordered the adult bookstore owner to cease operations. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the lower court. The court held that the adult bookstore's failure to apply for a special exception was not a bar to the subsequent constitutional attack on the ordinance. While the court held that the ordinance was constitutional, the court held that the special exception provision (as applied to adult bookstores) was unconstitutional. Nevertheless, the court held that the unconstitutional special exception provision was severable from the remainder of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment in favor of the state.

 

1104 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Tatum v. Gigliotti


No. 200, September Term, 1989


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


80 Md. App. 559; 565 A.2d 354; 1989 Md. App. LEXIS 187



November 3, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Prince George's County, James Magruder Rea, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant personal representative of decedent appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland) granted in favor of appellee paramedic by a mistrial against the personal representative's wrongful death and survival action, which the paramedic defended on the basis of civil immunity pursuant to Maryland's Good Samaritan Statute (Statute), Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 5-309.


OVERVIEW: The decedent suffered an asthma attack and called for emergency assistance from the paramedic who attempted to administer oxygen during their ambulance ride. After the decedent expired following hospital emergency room treatment, the personal representative filed a wrongful death and survival action against the paramedic and others dismissed from the lawsuit. Following the jury's failure to reach a verdict, the circuit court declared a mistrial and rendered judgment for the paramedic pursuant to his motion. The court affirmed this judgment contested by the personal representative and costs were imposed upon her. The court determined that, based on the legislative history and the facts, the statute's civil immunity applied to the paramedic as a salaried emergency medical technician who acted within the scope of his employment. The court held that, because no charge for services rendered was assessed upon decedent by the paramedic, who was a salaried personnel, the paramedic did not receive "compensation" under the Statute. The court found that the testimony indicated that although the paramedic's conduct might have constituted negligence, it did not qualify as gross negligence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court challenged by the personal representative entered into for the paramedic after the mistrial against the personal representative's wrongful death and a survival action, which the paramedic successfully opposed on the grounds of civil immunity under the statute.

 

1105 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Prince George's County v. Surratt


No. 102, September Term, 1989


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


80 Md. App. 415; 564 A.2d 95; 1989 Md. App. LEXIS 174



October 2, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Granted December 28, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] TWO APPEALS FROM THE Circuit Court for Prince George's County, Jacob S. Levin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The county and the parents both appealed from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), in a wrongful death and medical malpractice suit against a physician and the county. The jury found in favor of the physician but against the county and both parties accepted a remittitur as to the judgment awarded.


OVERVIEW: The parents' infant died shortly after he was born. They sued the county and the physician and the jury found in favor of the parents and the estate. The county contended that the claims of medical malpractice and wrongful death were barred by governmental immunity. The court agreed and reversed the decision of the trial court on the issue of governmental immunity, and thus did not address other issues that were raised on appeal. The county adopted a charter form of government. Prince George's County, Md. Charter § 1013 (1971) provided that the county waived its governmental immunity and could be sued in tort in the same manner and to the same extent as any private person. The charter was amended to provide a limited waiver of immunity by restricting the county's liability to those instances where its officers, agents and employees had no individual immunity. The court found that § 1013 was invalid in its entirety and the county's immunity barred the present challenge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

1106 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Board of County Comm'rs v. East Prince Frederick Corp.


No. 1654, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


80 Md. App. 78; 559 A.2d 822; 1989 Md. App. LEXIS 138



June 30, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Granted November 13, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Calvert County, John Hanson Briscoe, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board of county commissioners (county) challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Calvert County (Maryland), which held, in an action for declaratory and injunctive relief brought by appellee developer that the county's application of a time limit or minimum user fees to the developer violated the developer's rights under U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 (Contract Clause).


OVERVIEW: In 1978, the developer paid $ 11,000 to reserve 4,400 gallons of water and sewage usage capacity from the county. In 1983, the county imposed a "use it or lose it" policy by which party must either use its reserved allocation or alternatively pay minimum user fees, or forfeit the allocation. The developer sued for relief from the policy. The trial court found for the developer, holding that the policy substantially impaired the 1978 contract between the developer and the county, in violation of the Contract Clause. On appeal, the court held that the policy was constitutional, because the Contract Clause did not require a state (or subdivision thereof) to adhere in perpetuity to a contract which effectively surrendered an essential attribute of its sovereignty; in this case, the valid legislative concern with efficient allocation of the very limited sewer capacity existing in the county. The court also noted that the developer could easily maintain its rights by paying reasonable user fees, and therefore the impairment of the contract was not a substantial one, but one which was reasonable and necessary.


OUTCOME: The court held that the county's policy was not unconstitutional, nor did it substantially impair the contract, and accordingly reversed the trial court's judgment .

 

1107 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Potomac Elec. Power Co. v. Smith


No. 1395, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


79 Md. App. 591; 558 A.2d 768; 1989 Md. App. LEXIS 125



June 8, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] TWO APPEALS FROM THE Circuit Court for Prince George's County, Jacob S. Levin, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED: ONE-THIRD COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES. TWO-THIRDS COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee decedent and appellant electric company sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which granted judgment in favor of appellee in a suit involving wrongful death, the duty owed to trespassers, and a power company's liability for bodily harm to trespassers.


OVERVIEW: Appellee died when she touched appellant's downed power line. Appellant was aware that the power line was down and that the public continuously trespassed near the fallen line. The court affirmed the judgment in favor of appellee. The court held that a power company was subject to liability for bodily harm to trespassers if it knew, or should have known, that trespassers constantly intruded upon a limited area of the land, maintained a highly dangerous condition that was likely to cause death or serious bodily harm to such trespassers in that area, the trespassers were not likely to uncover the condition, and the company failed to exercise reasonable care to warn trespassers of the condition. The court held that appellee was not contributorily negligent because appellant failed to show a prominent or decisive act by appellee that directly contributed to the accident. The court held that the malice requirement for punitive damages was satisfied by appellant's wanton or reckless disregard for human life. The court held that appellee's recovery could be statutorily limited because the legislature had the power to completely eliminate her cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of appellee because appellant engaged in willful and wanton conduct by failing to exercise ordinary care once it knew or should have known of appellee's presence and the downed wire. Appellee was not contributorily negligent. Punitive damages were constitutional. Appellee's damages could be limited because the legislature could have eliminated her entire cause of action.

 

1108 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Fowler v. State


No. 1243, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


79 Md. App. 517; 558 A.2d 446; 1989 Md. App. LEXIS 115



June 6, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended June 23, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore County, John Grason Turnbull, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by a jury in the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) for first degree murder. He argued that the trial court erred in refusing to suppress evidence of his confession. He also argued that the search and seizure of his parked vehicle was unlawful and that the sentence imposed was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed that defendant knew the victim. Defendant was seen leaving the victim's apartment with another man carrying a knife. Defendant's car was seen outside the victim's home. The jury found defendant guilty of first degree murder. On appeal, the court ruled that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress his confession because a detective's statement to defendant that he should disclose the identity of his companion so that he could "share the weight" of the crime was not an inducement. The court ruled that defendant presented no evidence of coercion. The court also held that the officer's search of defendant's car was lawful because the police were not required to secure a warrant for the vehicle even though they had time to do so because the officers saw blood on the seat of the car. The court ruled that the seizure was lawful to secure the fruits of the crime. The court further ruled that the trial court properly denied defendant's requested jury instruction because the instructions given adequately explained the law of aiders and abettors. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and ruled that the sentence was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of first degree murder and ordered that costs be paid by defendant.

Board of County Comm'rs v. Gardner


No. 610, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


79 Md. App. 417; 557 A.2d 260; 1989 Md. App. LEXIS 109



May 3, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended June 29, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for St. Mary's County, Audrey E. Melbourne, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ST. MARY'S COUNTY VACATED AND CASE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board of county commissioners challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for St. Mary's County (Maryland) that was entered for appellee property owners in their action challenging the constitutionality of a county ordinance that levied a road tax on the property within a certain subdivision.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court declared the ordinance in question null and void, and the board appealed, asserting that the Maryland Attorney General was not notified of the circuit court proceedings as required by Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-405(c) (1974). The property owners asserted that it was unnecessary to comply with § 3-405(c) because the circuit court did not determine the statute to be unconstitutional, but struck it down for other reasons. The court vacated the judgment of the circuit court and remanded the case for further proceedings, holding that § 3-405(c) mandated the property owners to notify the Maryland Attorney General of the circuit court proceedings. The court further concluded that because all property owners in the affected subdivision were not joined in the action, the property owners were required to satisfy either the necessary joinder rules under Md. R. 2-211 or the class actions rules under Md. R. 2-231.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment that declared null and void the county ordinance that levied a road tax on the subdivision and remanded the case to the circuit court for further proceedings.

Department of Public Safety & Correctional Services v. Scruggs


No. 1083, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


79 Md. App. 312; 556 A.2d 736; 1989 Md. App. LEXIS 95



April 28, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County, James S. Sfekas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Public Safety and Correctional Services sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which reversed an administrative order sustaining the decision to remove appellee correctional officer from his position due to allegations of sexual misconduct with inmates.


OVERVIEW: The correctional officer was employed at a women's' correctional institute. An investigation revealed that three inmates had engaged in sexual encounters with the officer. All three inmates submitted to polygraph tests that indicated that their statements with regard to these encounters were truthful. Based on the statements, the results of the polygraph tests and other evidence with regard to the officer's schedule, the prison warden sought the officer's removal from state service. An administrative hearing resulted in a recommendation of removal, and the charges were sustained in an exceptions hearing. On the officer's appeal, the trial court reversed the administrative order, concluding that the polygraph evidence was improperly admitted at the administrative hearing. Upon review, the court affirmed the trial court's decision, holding that polygraph tests were so unreliable that the tests were deemed incompetent and should not have been admitted, even at an administrative hearing. The court found that the overriding question in the case was the inmates' credibility and under those circumstances, the admission of the polygraph evidence was not harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to reverse the administrative determination to remove the correctional officer from his employment due to allegations of sexual misconduct.

 

1111 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Prince George's County Health Dep't v. Briscoe


No. 1139, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


79 Md. App. 325; 556 A.2d 742; 1989 Md. App. LEXIS 97



April 28, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Montgomery County, J. James McKenna, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED. THE PARTIES TO BEAR THEIR OWN COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff social workers filed an administrative action against defendants, county and state health departments, to reclassify their positions to make them equal to psychiatric nurses performing similar duties and for increased and retroactive pay. Defendants appealed from the judgment for the social workers entered by the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) in their action for judicial review of the decision rendered against them.


OVERVIEW: The social workers asserted entitlement to salary at the same grade level as psychiatric nurses employed at the same facilities because they did the same work. A Department of Personnel (DOP) hearing examiner concluded that the social workers failed to satisfy their burden of proving that the state violated any law or acted arbitrarily in denying a salary adjustment to establish parity. The trial court remanded the case with instructions to reclassify the social workers, without issuing an opinion or stating the ground for its decision. The court held that the DOP decision did not violate the social workers' constitutional rights to due process or equal protection because the social workers and nurses did not have identical qualifications. The trial court also erred in considering the reclassification issue because the social workers raised it for the first time at the circuit court level and lacked the required qualifications. The decision to allow social workers from a different facility to intervene was also erroneous because it deprived the DOP of the opportunity to hear evidence and make findings regarding another facility. The attorney's fees award also had no legal basis.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that overturned the DOP decision rendered against the social workers in their grievance action for reclassification and increased and retroactive salary. The court also reversed the social workers' award of attorney's fees.

 

1112 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Crowder v. Baltimore


No. 999, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


79 Md. App. 291; 556 A.2d 726; 1989 Md. App. LEXIS 89



April 27, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City, Meyer M. Cardin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which affirmed the decision of a hearing examiner for the Employees' Retirement System of Baltimore City that found that the claimant was eligible for Ordinary Disability Retirement because he had not incurred a 75 percent anatomical loss of the use of his back.


OVERVIEW: The claimant contended that he was eligible for an Accidental Disability Retirement because he was 100 percent disabled from doing his job. He sustained a herniated disc in his back. The results of a physical examination established that he could no longer perform his job duties. He was terminated and awarded Ordinary Disability Retirement. The claimant argued that Baltimore City, MD., Code art. 22, § 9(j)(3) was unconstitutional because the 75 percent anatomical loss requirement to qualify for Accidental Disability Retirement was arbitrary and violated his equal protection and due process rights. Upon review, the court affirmed. It found that classification system was a reasonably based attempt to structure compensation benefits in accordance with the severity of the injuries sustained. The court found that defendant city's position that the claimant did not meet the 75 percent criterion, but was 100 percent impaired from performing his job functions was not inconsistent as loss of capacity to perform a job and anatomic disability were not the same.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that the claimant was only eligible for Ordinary Disability Retirement because he had not incurred a 75 percent anatomical loss of the use of his back.

McCormick Constr. Co. v. 9690 Deerco Rd. Ltd. Partnership


No. 1400, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


79 Md. App. 177; 556 A.2d 292; 1989 Md. App. LEXIS 85



April 6, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore County, John Grason Turnbull, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant subcontractor sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which stayed a mechanic's lien action filed by the subcontractor against appellee contractor pending arbitration of the disputes between the parties.


OVERVIEW: The subcontractor entered into a construction agreement with a contractor to build a parking deck. Four payments remained unpaid, and the contractor contested the amount due and alleged instances of faulty construction. A petition was filed, and the circuit court heard oral argument and concluded that, based on the arbitration clause in the parties' agreement, it had no discretion to continue once a petition to arbitrate was filed. The circuit court stayed the subcontractor's petition to establish a mechanic's lien, retained jurisdiction, and ordered arbitration. The subcontractor filed an appeal, which was dismissed by the court. The court held that the subcontractor had not established a right to appeal under Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 12-303, and, further, that the trial court had not entered a final judgment from which an appeal would lie. Also, the subcontractor's complaint that its priority among creditors might be jeopardized if it had to await a final judgment after arbitration before it could foreclose its lien had to be addressed by the General Assembly.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the subcontractor's appeal.

 

1114 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


318 North Market Street, Inc. v. Comptroller of Treasury


No. 1074, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


78 Md. App. 589; 554 A.2d 453; 1989 Md. App. LEXIS 65



March 8, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore City, Thomas Ward, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adult book store owner challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) that affirmed the tax court ruling in favor of appellee Maryland Comptroller of the Treasury subjecting "peep show" revenues to a 10 percent amusement and admission tax. The constitutionality of Md. Code Ann., Tax-Gen. § 4-102 also was challenged.


OVERVIEW: The book store owner displayed "peep shows" in private booths and the shows ran only after coins were deposited into boxes located in each booth. The Comptroller assessed back taxes against the book store owner after an audit revealed that he was paying admissions and amusement tax on the booth proceeds at an erroneous rate. He was paying five percent tax, when the correct rate was 10 percent. The Comptroller affirmed the assessment after a hearing and the tax court also upheld the levy. The circuit court affirmed the tax court decision. The court upheld the circuit court judgment, finding that the tax court correctly found that the "peep shows" were not movie theaters, within the meaning of City of Frederick, Md., Special Resolution 11-79 (1979), which imposed a five percent tax on theater admissions. The court also ruled that "peep show" equipment constituted recreational equipment, under Md. Code Ann., Tax-Gen. § 4-102(b). Therefore, the equipment was subject to the admissions and amusement tax and properly assessed at a 10 percent tax rate. Finally, the court declined to consider the claim that the definition of recreational equipment was unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1115 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Chan v. State


No. 754, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


78 Md. App. 287; 552 A.2d 1351; 1989 Md. App. LEXIS 158



February 7, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which convicted defendant of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, possession of drug paraphernalia, illegal gambling, and possession of a short-barreled shotgun.


OVERVIEW: The police obtained a court order to install a pen register on defendant's telephone number. The data recorded provided evidence of a gambling operation, which was the basis of the search warrant issued for defendant's residence. Defendant claimed that all of the evidence found in the search should have been suppressed because the warrant was the product of an unlawful trace on his telephone. The court affirmed defendant's convictions and held: 1) the trap and trace device used to record the originating phone number of all incoming calls did not implicate the Fourth Amendment expectation of privacy, which attached only to the content of the communication and not to the fact that the communication took place; 2) neither Title III of the Omnibus Crime Control and Safe Streets Act of 1968, codified as 18 U.S.C.S. §§ 2510-2521, nor the Maryland Wiretapping and Electronic Surveillance Statute, at Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 10-405, governed the use of pen registers because pen registers did not acquire the contents of communications; and 3)even if there had been a violation of the wiretapping statutes, the exclusion of the evidence would not have been a proper remedy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, possession of drug paraphernalia, illegal gambling, and possession of a short-barreled shotgun.

 

1116 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Rockville Crushed Stone, Inc. v. Montgomery County


No. 715, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


78 Md. App. 176; 552 A.2d 960; 1989 Md. App. LEXIS 43



February 3, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended February 9, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County William C. Miller, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant quarry company sought review of judgment from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) that affirmed Resolution 10-1971 (the Resolution) enacted by appellee county, which denied the quarry company's zoning application that sought a zoning reclassification.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the Resolution, the quarry company was denied a zoning application that sought a zoning reclassification from the Rural, Rural Density Transfer, and R-200 zones to the Mineral Resource Recovery Zone in order to conduct quarrying operations on its property. The quarry company claimed that the county acted arbitrarily, capriciously, and illegally in denying its application. The court affirmed the denial. The court held that the county's denial of the zoning application was not arbitrary, capricious, or illegal. The court found that the quarry company had failed to satisfy the "Master Plan" requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court that affirmed the county's decision to deny the application of the quarry company for a zoning reclassification of its property.

 

1117 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


AMI Operating Partners Ltd. Partnership v. JAD Enterprises, Inc.


No. 544, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


77 Md. App. 654; 551 A.2d 888; 1989 Md. App. LEXIS 14



January 9, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied March 8, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: TWO APPEALS FROM THE Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County, Robert S. Heise, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART; CASE REMANDED TO CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY FOR MODIFICATION OF JUDGMENT IN ACCORDANCE WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE PAID ONE-HALF BY APPELLANTS, ONE-HALF BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) that declared that appellee contractor was entitled to a mechanics' lien on certain property owned by the property owner. The contractor brought a petition for the lien, and the court, after denying the property owner's motion to dismiss the petition, had entered a final order establishing the amount of the lien.


OVERVIEW: The property owner argued that Maryland mechanics' lien law deprived property owners of their property without due process of law, allowed the state to engage in a "taking" of private property for a private use, and that the trial court erred in admitting into evidence certain invoices. The court affirmed, in part, and reversed, in part. The court found that Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 9-105 provided sufficient notice to a property owner and afforded him a hearing and, therefore, did not deprive an owner of property without due process of law. The court found no merit to the property owner's argument that law permitted the state to take personal property explaining that the state wasn't "taking" the debtor's property for either public or private use but merely creating an orderly process for the satisfaction of a debt that had been found by a court to be due and owing. The court found that the contractor failed to attach several invoices to his lien petition as required by § 9-105 and that the invoices were material. The court concluded that the defect did not negate entire lien but remanded the case so that the amount of the invoices could be deducted from the lien calculations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, in part, reversed it, in part, and remanded the case for a modification of the judgment in accordance with the opinion.

Village Square No. 1, Inc. v. Crow-Frederick Retail Ltd. Partnership


No. 457, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


77 Md. App. 552; 551 A.2d 471; 1989 Md. App. LEXIS 7



January 5, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Frederick County, G. Edward Dwyer, Jr., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant development corporations challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Frederick County (Maryland) that declared City of Frederick, Md., Code § 22-35 (amended 1988) invalid because it contained no due process protections for parties who were potentially liable for the cost of public improvements. The development corporations sought reimbursement from appellees, the development partnerships and the City of Frederick, Md.


OVERVIEW: The parties were developers and owners of property in the early stages of subdivision construction. The development corporation spent $ 700,000 on public improvements required under City of Frederick, Md., Subdivision Reg. § 2(g). Two years later, City of Frederick, Md., Code § 22-35 (amended 1988), which was the was amended to permit recovery of the proportionate share of the costs of improvements utilized by other property owners. When the development corporations sought recoupment of a share of the costs from the development partnerships, the circuit court granted the motion for summary judgment filed by the City and the development partnerships. The circuit court held that the amended portion of the section was invalid because it did not contain due process protections for the potentially liable parties. The court affirmed the judgment, finding that the amendment imposed liabilities that warranted imposition of due process requirements, whether it was deemed a "special exaction" or a "special benefit assessment." The court noted that no notice or hearing, assessment, or appeal procedures were provided in the amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Allnut v. Comptroller of Treasury


No. 243, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


77 Md. App. 424; 550 A.2d 728; 1988 Md. App. LEXIS 242



December 6, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied March 8, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Howard County, Cornelius F. Sybert, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; PURSUANT TO MD. RULE 1-341 LOWELL H. BECRAFT, JR., JAMES L. MAYER AND THE APPELLANTS ARE JOINTLY AND SEVERALLY ORDERED TO PAY TO THE STATE OF MARYLAND THE SUM OF $ 1,275 AND THE COSTS OF THESE PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Howard County (Maryland), which dismissed their suit against respondent seeking to enjoin the assessment and collection of state personal income taxes.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners alleged that the state income taxes were invalid because they were based on a federal constitutional amendment, which was never ratified, so they filed a suit against respondent seeking to enjoin the assessment and collection of the taxes. The trial court dismissed the suit, and on appeal, the court affirmed holding that the state's taxing power was a basic attribute of sovereignty. The court further held that the federal government's taxing power was different and was derived from the people. The court also held that Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 280(a) (1957, 1980 Repl.Vol.), the state personal income tax statute, was only dependent on the federal income tax for calculation purposes and not as the source of the state's taxing power. Finally, the court held that because of prior decisions rejecting arguments similar to those of petitioners, sanctions against petitioners were warranted pursuant to Md. R. 1-341.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order of the trial court, which dismissed petitioners' suit against respondent seeking to enjoin the assessment and collection of state personal income taxes. The court also sanctioned petitioners for the filing of the baseless suit.

Gardner v. State


No. 283, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


77 Md. App. 237; 549 A.2d 1171; 1988 Md. App. LEXIS 225



November 14, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THECircuit Court for Anne Arundel County, Eugene M. Lerner, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COST TO BE PAID ONE-HALF BY APPELLANTS, ONE-HALF BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant residents sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which granted the motion of appellee State of Maryland (state) to dismiss the residents' action for damages for injuries caused by the state's maintenance of a nuisance due to noise and "repellant odors" caused by low-flying aircraft at a nearby airport and two public highways, and negligent operation of the airport in general.


OVERVIEW: The residents filed their action against the state days before the legislature enacted the State Tort Claims Act (Act), Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 12-101 -- 12-109, which required claimants to show that they had sent notice to the state treasurer and received a denial therefrom prior to bringing suit. Initially, they alleged that they did not have to comply with the Act because, they argued, their claims were based on a theory of inverse condemnation. Thereafter, they amended the complaint to allege compliance with the Act to obtain the benefit of the initial date of filing, at which time there was no cap on damages in an action against the state. The trial court granted the state's motion to dismiss based on the residents' failure to comply with the notice requirements of the Act. On appeal, the court ruled that the trial court should have permitted the residents to amend their complaint to allege compliance with the Act rather than dismiss the suit, however, the residents' complaint would not obtain the benefit of the original date of filing. The court held that to apply the "relation back" doctrine would have rendered meaningless the notice requirements under the Act.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order dismissing the residents' amended complaint and remanded the case for further proceedings.

Harris v. Housing Authority of Baltimore City


No. 201, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


77 Md. App. 160; 549 A.2d 770; 1988 Md. App. LEXIS 214



November 7, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended November 10, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore City, Marvin B. Steinberg, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE DIVIDED EQUALLY BETWEEN THE PARTIES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellant tenant requested a jury trial, the district court ordered her to pay rent into an escrow account pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 8-118, and forwarded appellee Housing Authority of Baltimore City (landlord)'s holding over/breach of lease action to the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland). The tenant did not escrow the rent. The circuit court awarded the authority a judgment and possession. The tenant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landlord terminated the tenant's lease because it believed the tenant was allowing her son to sell drugs on the premises. The tenant argued on appeal that the circuit court erred in holding that she had waived her right to a jury trial and denied her the opportunity to litigate the underlying claim when it summarily entered judgment for the landlord after it found that she had not escrowed the rent. The court held that the tenant waived her right to a jury trial because the escrow order was valid and the tenant's failure to comply with it was not legally justified. The court held that the escrow order did not incorporate the terms of the tenant's lease, which allowed for the late payment of rent in hardship circumstances and that, even if it did, the tenant did not comply with the notice provisions of the lease. The court agreed that the tenant was entitled to litigate the merits of the underlying dispute because due process required a hearing and proof of good cause for eviction, a hearing was required under Md. R. Civ. P., Cir. Ct. 2-311(f), and the hearing on the escrow order's validity and the tenant's compliance was not a trial on the merits of the underlying dispute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the judgment which held that the tenant waived her right to a jury trial. The court vacated the circuit court's order for a judgment and warrant of possession in favor of the landlord and remanded the case for a hearing on the merits of the underlying dispute between the parties.

 

1122 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Desser v. Department of Health & Mental Hygiene


No. 5, September Term, 1988


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


77 Md. App. 1; 549 A.2d 18; 1988 Md. App. LEXIS 207



November 1, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended December 21, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Appeals from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City, David Ross, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE DIVIDED EQUALLY BETWEEN THE PARTIES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which affirmed the Secretary of Personnel's decision reinstating the employee without backpay at appellee agency.


OVERVIEW: The agency hearing officer recommended discharging the employee for practicing law on state time. The employee filed exceptions and a hearing was held before the Secretary. The Secretary reinstated the employee without backpay. A four and one-half year period elapsed between the time the employee was discharged and his reinstatement. The employee and the agency appealed the Secretary's decision to the circuit court, which affirmed the Secretary's decision. Both parties appealed. The employee argued that the delay between his discharge and reinstatement deprived him of due process of law. The court held that the agency was not accountable for the period in which the circuit court exercised exclusive jurisdiction over the proceedings and found that the only period of delay that was attributable to the agency was the period from the date of the hearing before the Secretary to the time of the Secretary's final decision: seven months and eleven days. The court found that this delay was not a due process violation because its length was not unreasonable and the employee was not prejudiced. The court affirmed the circuit court's decision affirming the Secretary's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court which affirmed the Secretary's decision reinstating the employee without backpay during the four and one-half year pendency of his claim challenging his dismissal from the agency.
