Tereshuk v. State


No. 578, September Term, 1985


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


66 Md. App. 193; 503 A.2d 254; 1986 Md. App. LEXIS 245



January 17, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied May 2, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County, David L. Cahoon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which convicted defendant of driving while under the influence of alcohol. Defendant entered into a plea arrangement whereby the State agreed to amend its charging document to allege driving while under the influence of alcohol, a lesser offense than driving while intoxicated. Defendant, for his part, agreed to plead guilty to the amended charge.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that defendant's prior convictions for driving while his driving ability was impaired by the consumption of alcohol brought defendant within the purview of the "subsequent offender" provision, Md. Code Ann., Transp. I § 27-101(f). The issue before the court was whether a person convicted of "driving while under the influence of alcohol," Md. Code Ann., Transp. I § 21-902(b), could be sentenced as a "second or subsequent offender" under Md. Code Ann., Transp. I § 27-101(f) when the repeat offender treatment was based on prior convictions for "driving while ability impaired by alcohol" (former Md. Code Ann., Transp. I § 21-902(b)). Defendant claimed that "driving while under the influence of alcohol" and "driving while ability impaired by alcohol" could not be treated as interchangeable because they were entirely different crimes. The court held that defendant was properly sentenced as a subsequent offender under Md. Code Ann., Transp. I § 27-101(f). The court held that 1981 Md. Laws 242, § 2 explicitly stated that "driving under the influence of alcohol" should have the same meaning and effect as its precursor, "driving while ability impaired by alcohol."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Parker v. State


No. 13, September Term, 1985


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


66 Md. App. 1; 502 A.2d 510; 1986 Md. App. LEXIS 230



January 10, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied April 18, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City, Marshal Levin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) in which he was found guilty of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute. He contended that the court erred in denying his motion to suppress the drugs and money seized from his pocket and from a car.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 26-202(a)(2)(ii) (1984 Repl. Vol., 1985 Supp.), which authorized a warrantless arrest if an officer had reasonable grounds to believe that a person would disregard a traffic citation, a police officer arrested defendant after concluding that he was operating a motor vehicle without an operator's license. On appeal, the court held that the arrest was lawful, where it was not unreasonable for the officer to place weight on the nervous behavior of defendant, on the only type of identification presented by defendant -- a prison I.D. card, and on the conduct of defendant in exiting the car in a manner which caused the police officer to believe he would flee. The court held that the search of the vehicle was legal, where, having validly arrested the defendant, the officer proceeded to make a lawful search of defendant's person incident to the prior lawful arrest. His observation on defendant's person of what he believed to be cocaine thereafter placed the officer in a position where he had the legal right to search the automobile, particularly since he had earlier observed defendant conceal a bag within the console of that vehicle.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

 

1167 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Greenberg v. State


No. 381, September Term, 1985


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


66 Md. App. 24; 502 A.2d 522; 1986 Md. App. LEXIS 240



January 10, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied March 24, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County, Eugene M. Lerner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which granted summary judgment to appellee state aviation administration and held that their property had not been "taken" by application of state noise regulations.


OVERVIEW: The landowners alleged that the combined effect of the state's airport noise zone regulations and the county zoning ordinance was to "severely diminish" the value of their property. Based upon that premise, they argued that their property has been unconstitutionally taken without compensation. In affirming the decision, the court differentiated between a "taking", which deprived the owner of all reasonable uses of his land, and "police powers", which only affected the owners' use and enjoyment. Before a court could conclude there had been an unconstitutional taking of the property, the government regulation had to deprive the landowner of all reasonable uses of his land. Here, the landowners alleged that the combined effect of the state regulation, which limited what could be built in the presence of the airport noise, and the county zoning ordinance, which limited the density and uses of the property, severely diminished the value of the vacant properties. However, this diminution of value did not constitute a taking, and summary judgment was properly granted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision which granted summary judgment to the state and held that the zoning and noise regulations did not constitute a taking.

 

1168 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Welsh v. Department of Natural Resources


No. 349, September Term, 1985


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


65 Md. App. 710; 501 A.2d 1351; 1986 Md. App. LEXIS 226



January 9, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two Appeals From The Circuit Court for Allegany County, Gary G. Leasure, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR THE PASSAGE OF A DECREE NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court for Allegany County (Maryland), which found in favor of appellee Department of Natural Resources in an action by the property owner for a declaration that he owned a 33 acre tract of land in fee simple in the 1132 acre tract of land taken by the State by condemnation and sought to enjoin the Department from asserting a claim to the 33 acre tract.


OVERVIEW: The Department successfully filed condemnation proceedings against the 1132 acre tract in 1966 for public use as a State park. In 1983 the property owner filed an action alleging that that he was the owner of a 33 acre tract located within the perimeter lines of the lands described in the condemnation proceedings. The property owner asserted that neither he nor his predecessor in title were parties to the condemnation proceedings and were not given condemnation notice. On appeal, the court determined that the record supported the conclusion that the record title of the property owner was paramount to the title of the condemnation parties who claimed title to the full 1132 acre tract. Where the party in interest was not named in the petition for condemnation, the proceedings were not binding on him unless the omitted party in some way waived the defect. The property owner received no notice and did not waive the defect. As applied to the 33 acre tract, the condemnation proceedings were void to the extent that they purported to affect the land of the property owner, his title, or possessory rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded with directions for the passage of a decree not inconsistent with its opinion.

 

1169 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Doctors' Hospital of Prince George's County v. Maryland Health Resources Planning Com.


No. 318, September Term, 1985


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


65 Md. App. 656; 501 A.2d 1324; 1986 Md. App. LEXIS 227



January 8, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City, Robert I. H. Hammerman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which affirmed the decision of appellee Maryland Health Resources Planning Commission (commission) to deny its application for a certificate of need (CON) to permit an increase in its bed capacity.


OVERVIEW: The commission denied a hospital's application for a CON to permit additional beds. The circuit court affirmed. On appeal, the court affirmed because substantial evidence supported the decision that the application was inconsistent with seven criteria under Md. Regs. Code tit. 10, § 24.01.06B(2). The court found that the commission properly weighed present and future utilization factors in its need analysis and found that increasing utilization at existing facilities was a less costly alternative and that the hospital failed to show volume changes in ancillary services or meet the needs of the underserved. The commission did not review by ambush the financial feasibility criterion and properly rejected the uncontradicted statement that the hospital would raise the necessary financing. The court held that the decision that additional beds could not be certified until completion of a location analysis was not an illegal moratorium on CONs. The court found that the commission did not arbitrarily discriminate by granting the application of another hospital with a present need for additional beds because the cases were not decided on basically the same evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, with the hospital to pay costs, the decision upholding the commission's denial of the CON application.

 

1170 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Rowe v. Chesapeake & Potomac Tel. Co.


No. 386, September Term, 1985


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


65 Md. App. 527; 501 A.2d 464; 1985 Md. App. LEXIS 509



December 11, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County, William Cave, Judge.



DISPOSITION: INJUNCTION AFFIRMED. DECLARATORY JUDGMENT VACATED AND CASE REMANDED FOR ENTRY OF DECLARATORY JUDGMENT IN CONFORMANCE WITH THIS OPINION. APPELLANTS TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant intervenors sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which entered judgment in favor of appellee telephone company, in a complaint by the telephone company seeking an injunction against the implementation of a county charter restricting the county's ability to contract with the telephone company.


OVERVIEW: Montgomery County, Md., Charter § 313A, was created by an initiative petition and restricted public contracts with the telephone company. The telephone company filed a complaint seeking a declaratory judgment and an injunction. The county consented to the injunction, but appellants intervened on behalf of the county. Declaratory judgment was entered in favor of the telephone company and an injunction was issued on the ground that the charter was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed the issuance of the injunction, but modified the declaratory judgment. The court held that the existence of the intervenors established an actual controversy capable of being resolved by a declaratory judgment. The court further held that while the injunction was properly issued, the proper ground for its issuance was not the unconstitutionality of the charter, but the narrower ground that the charter conflicted with a public law, Md. Ann. Code art. 78, § 26.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the injunction issued in favor of the telephone company, but vacated and remanded for the entry of the declaratory judgment in conformance with the court's decision.

 

1171 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Teeter v. State


No. 119, September Term, 1985


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


65 Md. App. 105; 499 A.2d 503; 1985 Md. App. LEXIS 482



November 7, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied January 30, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Carroll County, H. Chester Goudy, Jr., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: DAYTIME HOUSEBREAKING: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. THEFT AND MALICIOUS DESTRUCTION OF PROPERTY: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED AND SENTENCES VACATED AND REMANDED FOR IMPOSITION OF A LEGAL SENTENCE. COSTS TO BE PAID 4/5 BY APPELLANT AND 1/5 BY CARROLL COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for malicious destruction of property and the concurrent, mandatory 25-year sentences imposed against him by the Circuit Court for Carroll County (Maryland) for that conviction, as well as for his convictions for daytime housebreaking and theft.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of daytime housebreaking, theft, and malicious destruction of property. At sentencing the trial court imposed concurrent, mandatory 25-year sentences on all three convictions under the multiple offender statute, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 643B. Defendant appealed the malicious destruction of property conviction and the sentences. The court affirmed the conviction and the sentence for daytime housebreaking. The court, however, vacated the other sentences. The record did not support an inference that the door to the dwelling was broken in a negligent manner. Thus, there was sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction for malicious destruction of property. Otherwise inadmissible hearsay was admissible for sentencing purposes. Regardless, the evidence objected to was merely cumulative, and its admission was harmless. Since a crime of violence for purposes of § 643B was defined to include daytime housebreaking, proof of defendant's conviction alone was sufficient. Neither theft nor malicious destruction of property were enumerated crimes of violence within the enhanced punishment statute. Hence, the sentences for those offenses were illegal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for malicious destruction of property and the 25-year sentence for his daytime housebreaking conviction. The court, however, vacated the sentences for defendant's theft and malicious destruction of property convictions and remanded the case for resentencing.

 

1172 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Randall Book Corp. v. State


No. 52, September Term, 1985


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


64 Md. App. 589; 497 A.2d 1174; 1985 Md. App. LEXIS 528



October 4, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who operated a bookstore, appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which convicted him for obscenity offenses for exhibiting materials for advertising purposes in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 416D.


OVERVIEW: The detectives obtained a warrant to enter and search defendant's premises and to seize and remove all books, magazines, and other materials displayed for advertising purposes that depicted sadomasochistic abuse, sexual conduct, and sexual excitement. Defendant claimed that the statute was unconstitutional and that there was insufficient probable cause for the issuance of the warrant, so evidence should have been suppressed. On review, the court found no error by the trial court in convicting defendant on numerous counts and imposing a fine for each conviction. The court concluded that the massive seizure of hundreds of books, magazines and films from defendant's bookstore was lawful and that the statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad in its application. There was probable cause to believe that defendant was violating art. 27, § 416D by displaying in its store, for purpose of advertising, material proscribed by the statute. Thus, the objective good faith of the officers in executing this warrant rendered any defect in the warrant irrelevant. The trial court did not err in refusing to suppress the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments.

 

1173 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Leese v. Baltimore County


No. 1599, September Term, 1984


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


64 Md. App. 442; 497 A.2d 159; 1985 Md. App. LEXIS 469



September 9, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Baltimore County Austin W. Brizendine, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART. CASE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID ONE-HALF BY APPELLANT AND ONE-HALF BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which dismissed appellant's multi-count amended declaration against appellees, county and supervisors, for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted.


OVERVIEW: After his dismissal, appellant former employee brought a lawsuit against appellees, county and supervisors, alleging a number of constitutional and common law infractions. A trial court dismissed appellant's multi-count amended declaration against appellees for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in part and reversed in part. The court could not find any allegation in appellant's amended declaration that he was entitled to a merit position. The court found that appellant had not shown that his liberty interest in future employment was abridged. However, appellant adequately alleged that his challenge to the hiring process was a motivating factor in appellees' decision to dismiss him. Thus, appellant's amended declaration was sufficient to charge abusive discharge against all appellees. The court held that appellant's amended declaration sufficiently set forth a cause of action in libel per quod, and that appellant sufficiently alleged all the elements of defamation. The court concluded that actual malice was alleged by appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part a trial court's judgment dismissing appellant former employee's multi-count amended declaration against appellees, county and supervisors, for failure to state a claim because appellant had not shown that he was entitled to a merit position or that his liberty interest in future employment was abridged, but appellant sufficiently charged abusive discharge, libel per quod, and defamation.

Lucky Ned Pepper's, Ltd. v. Columbia Park & Recreation Asso.


No. 1508, September Term, 1984


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


64 Md. App. 222; 494 A.2d 947; 1985 Md. App. LEXIS 459



July 10, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HOWARD COUNTY Eugene M. Lerner (specially assigned) JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO CIRCUIT COURT FOR HOWARD COUNTY FOR HEARING ON MOTION FOR JUDGMENT AND FOR SUCH OTHER AND FURTHER PROCEEDINGS THAT ARE CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; 1/2 COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE; 1/2 COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tenant challenged the judgment from the Circuit Court for Howard County (Maryland), which ruled that Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 8-118 (1981 Repl. Vol., 1984 Cum. Supp.) was constitutional, held that the tenant's due process rights were not violated, granted appellee landlord's motion for judgment, and denied the tenant's motion to strike the district court order.


OVERVIEW: The landlord filed a suit in district court against the tenant requesting possession of and accrued rent on the area of the golf course clubhouse occupied by the tenant's bar and restaurant. The action was filed under Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 8-401, which provided for summary eviction proceedings based upon the tenant's failure to pay rent. Pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 8-118 (1981 Repl. Vol., 1984 Cum. Supp.), the tenant was required to pay the accrued rents into an escrow account. The court vacated and remanded the circuit court order that affirmed the district court orders. The court concluded that: (1) to the extent that § 8-118 provided for payment of past due rent into escrow, it was an unconstitutional infringement of the tenant's right to a civil jury trial; (2) § 8-118 was reasonable to the extent that it provided for payment into an escrow account of rents accruing during trial; (3) § 8-118 when read in conjunction with Md. R. Civ. P. 2-311(f) provided the tenant with the opportunity for a hearing prior to requiring an escrow of the funds; and (4) the district court had the jurisdiction to order the escrow payment notwithstanding the prayer for a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and remanded the circuit court judgment that had been entered in favor of the landlord.

Alban v. Board of Education


No. 1440, September Term, 1984


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


64 Md. App. 169; 494 A.2d 745; 1985 Md. App. LEXIS 454



July 8, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 21, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HARFORD COUNTY CYPERT O. WHITFILL, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the parents of a handicapped child, filed suit against defendants, the Board of Education and their child's physical education instructor, and alleged that their child, who sustained injuries during a physical education class, should not have been placed in a regular physical education program. The Circuit Court for Harford County (Maryland) granted defendants' motion for a directed verdict. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parents' handicapped child was injured while participating in a regular physical education program. The parents filed suit against the board of education (board) and the physical education teacher (teacher) and claimed that their child should not have been placed in a regular physical education class. The trial court entered a directed verdict in favor of the board and the teacher. The parents appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the trial court properly excluded evidence relating to the board's evaluation and placement of the child because the parents had approved the individual education program formulated by the board. According to the court, absent the exhaustion of administrative remedies, the parents' claim of negligent placement was not properly before the trial court. In addition, the court rejected the parents' claim that the application of Md. Code Ann., Educ. § 8-415 denied them their constitutional rights to seek redress for their child's injuries. The court found that the parents could have alleged, but did not allege, that the teacher or board failed to exercise reasonable care to protect their child from injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment entered in favor of the Board of Education and the physical education instructor on the complaint filed by the parents of a handicapped child, who was injured while participating in a regular physical education class.

 

1176 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Ungar v. State


No. 829, September Term, 1984


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


63 Md. App. 472; 492 A.2d 1336; 1985 Md. App. LEXIS 419



June 5, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY FRANK E. CICONE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) sustaining appellee State Department of Health and Mental Hygiene's (Department) preliminary objections and demurrer and dismissing the owner's claim alleging in part that the Department's sewer moratorium constituted a taking of his property without just compensation in violation of U.S. Const. amend. V.


OVERVIEW: A property owner filed suit against the State Department of Health and Mental Hygiene contending that a sewer moratorium and the resulting seven-month delay caused the owner to incur added costs in the construction of an automobile dealership. The owner contended the moratorium constituted a taking of his property without just compensation in violation of U.S. Const. amend. V. The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment dismissing the owner's action and concluded that that the moratorium had been imposed solely to prevent a public harm and not to unjustly discriminate against the owner. The court held that a seven-month delay in the construction was not unduly lengthy or burdensome and concluded that the moratorium imposition and its duration constituted neither a taking of private property without just compensation nor a deprivation of the owner's property without due process of law. The result was the same even if the test related only to the extent to which the use of the owner's property was restricted. The court also held the owner's cause was barred by a three-year statute of limitations since the suit was not filed until ten years after the imposition of the moratorium.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment dismissing the property owner's claim alleging that the Department's sewer moratorium constituted a taking of property without just compensation. The court concluded that the sewer moratorium was imposed to prevent a public harm and did not constitute a taking of the owner's property or a deprivation of such property.

 

1177 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Anaweck v. State


No. 1205, September Term, 1984


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


63 Md. App. 239; 492 A.2d 658; 1985 Md. App. LEXIS 407



May 17, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY WILLIAM R. BUCHANAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a decision by the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which convicted defendants of the unlawful possession of cocaine in sufficient quantity to indicate reasonably an intent to distribute.


OVERVIEW: Defendants contended that the trial judge erroneously permitted evidence of other criminal activity on the part of defendants; and that the evidence was not legally sufficient to support the convictions for possession with intent to distribute. The court held that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion in admitting the "other crimes" evidence. The state trooper's observations on December 10 and December 11 revealed that defendants had the motive. The state established intent to sell by proving that defendants were in the habit of selling. The observations of December 10 and December 11 removed all possibility of mistake. The evidence showed that defendants were the two involved in the illicit trafficking in narcotics and in the illicit possession of the contraband merchandise. To show on three successive days a sale, another sale, and the possession of merchandise for sale was evidence of "a common scheme." The "other crimes" evidence of December 10 and December 11 identified defendants as the possessors. The trial judge was not wrong in ruling that the evidence was legally sufficient to permit the case to go to the jury. Thus, the court affirmed the judgments of conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for the unlawful possession of cocaine in sufficient quantity to indicate reasonably an intent to distribute.

 

1178 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Bryan v. State


No. 1275, September Term, 1984


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


63 Md. App. 210; 492 A.2d 644; 1985 Md. App. LEXIS 397



May 15, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY A. OWEN HENNEGAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, defendant was convicted of burglary and theft. The State established that defendant had been convicted of two prior offenses, robbery with a deadly weapon and robbery. After a sentencing hearing on remand, the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) again sentenced defendant to a term of 25 years without parole pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 643B(c). Defendant appealed his sentence.


OVERVIEW: The theft conviction was merged with the burglary conviction. The Maryland "three-time loser" recidivist statute applied because defendant had been convicted of two prior crimes of violence as defined in Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 643B(a) and had served time in prison for one of those crimes. The court rejected defendant's contention that the recidivist statute was unconstitutional as violative of the Eighth Amendment. The court noted a plethora of recent state and federal district court cases upholding mandatory recidivist statutes. The court said that, in the interest of avoiding judicial intervention into legislative sentencing decisions, the United States Supreme Court upheld an imposition of a life sentence on one who had been convicted of three relatively minor non-violent crimes classified as felonies. The court said that defendant's sentence did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment and a proportionality review was not warranted. The court added that the Maryland statute, unlike other statutes found consistent with the Eight Amendment, did not mandate a life sentence for previous offenders. The court added that defendant had some hope of an eventual release from prison.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Miller v. Maloney Concrete Co.


No. 845, September Term, 1984


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


63 Md. App. 38; 491 A.2d 1218; 1985 Md. App. LEXIS 335



May 9, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY, JAMES S. McAULIFFE, JUDGE.
MILLER v. MALONEY CONCRETE CO., 1985 Md. App. LEXIS 363 (Md. Ct. Spec. App., Apr. 10, 1985)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which reversed the county board of appeals' decision that appellee concrete company's operation constituted a public nuisance and which held that Montgomery County, Md., Code § 59-A-5.7 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The property owner, pursuant to Montgomery County, Md., Code § 59-A-5.7, filed a petition with the county board of appeals (board) and claimed that the concrete company's business operations produced dust, dirt, noise, vibration, and smoke so as to affect adversely the public health, safety, and general welfare, as well as the peaceful use, enjoyment, and value of surrounding properties. The board found that the concrete company's business operations constituted a public nuisance. The concrete company appealed that decision to the circuit court. The circuit court reversed the board's decision and held that § 59-A-5.7 was unconstitutional. The property owner appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the circuit court's decision. The court found that § 59-A-5.7 was void for vagueness. According to the court, § 59-A-5.7 impermissibly permitted the board to subject the concrete company to criminal penalties for using its property in a manner that was otherwise lawful, and to do so in derogation of the jurisdiction carefully and expressly conferred on other agencies, all without any clear standards and upon evidence that in no way compelled the conclusions reached.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court entered in favor of the concrete company.

Ocean Plaza Joint Venture v. Crouse Constr. Co.


No. 642, September Term, 1984


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


62 Md. App. 435; 490 A.2d 252; 1985 Md. App. LEXIS 359



April 8, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR WORCESTER COUNTY DALE R. CATHELL, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED FOR NEW TRIAL. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner sought review of a decree from the Circuit Court for Worcester County (Maryland), which established a final mechanics' lien in favor of appellee subcontractor and which ordered the sale of the owner's property unless the lien was paid.


OVERVIEW: The subcontractor performed the excavation and grading portion of a project on property of the owner. The subcontractor performed additional work, but executed general release and waiver forms for an amount that did not include charges for the additional work. The subcontractor filed a mechanics' lien for an amount including the additional work. At a hearing, the trial court refused to consider the release and waiver forms because the owner did not plead waiver in its answer. The trial court entered a decree to enforce the lien including the additional work. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the trial court properly refused to consider a waiver defense that was not raised in the pleadings. However, the court held that the release and waiver forms were admissible to the extent that they were relevant on the issue of the proper amount of the lien, which was contested in the pleadings and at the hearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court' decree entering a final mechanics' lien in favor of the subcontractor and ordering the sale of the owner's property if the lien was not paid, and the court remanded the case for a new trial.

 

1181 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Anne Arundel County v. Ebersberger


No. 991, September Term, 1984


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


62 Md. App. 360; 489 A.2d 96; 1985 Md. App. LEXIS 344



March 15, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY, RAYMOND G. THIEME, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO DISMISS BILL OF COMPLAINT, AS AMENDED; COSTS TO BE DIVIDED ONE-HALF TO APPELLANT, ONE-HALF TO APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which entered a judgment for plaintiff homeowners in their declaratory judgment action challenging a county ordinance that required all the property owners in the community to pay for the reconstruction and maintenance of a pool. The trial court held that the ordinance was ultra vires and therefore invalid.


OVERVIEW: A majority of the homeowners in a community persuaded the county government to enact an ordinance requiring all the property owners in the community to pay for the reconstruction and maintenance of the pool through annual special benefit taxes levied against their property. Four of the homeowners challenged the ordinance as being both ultra vires and unconstitutional in a bill for declaratory judgment. The trial court declared the ordinance invalid on the basis that the ordinance was ultra vires because the ordinance did not represent a valid exercise of the county's authority under Md. Code Ann. art. 25A, § 5. The county appealed, and the court vacated the judgment and remanded for dismissal of the complaint, holding that an actual, justiciable controversy did not exist, and therefore the homeowners' complaint should not have been ruled upon at all, but dismissed. The court held that the homeowners had suffered no injury from the challenged ordinance because the ordinance did not require the county to renovate the pool, nor did it specify any particular means of financing the renovation.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the trial court that the ordinance was ultra vires and invalid, and remanded to the trial court for dismissal of the homeowner's complaint.

Anderson v. State


No. 77, September Term, 1984


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


61 Md. App. 436; 487 A.2d 294; 1985 Md. App. LEXIS 310



February 6, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY MARY ARABIAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) convicted defendant of common law assault and battery (common law) but not statutory child abuse of his infant son. Defendant contended that the common law had been repealed by the Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 35A (1957) of the Child Abuse Law (statute), that error existed admitting a prior carrying a handgun conviction, and that the trial judge inhibited the offering of the defense's character evidence.


OVERVIEW: Whether the enactment of the child abuse statute preempted a particular corner of the field of common law assault and battery and repealed it was at issue. The court found that every use of excessive or immoderate force that would have defeated the common law privilege and thereby rendered the accused guilty of the common law crime, would, ipso facto, have rendered the accused guilty under the statute. The court concluded that the statute did not preempt the field and, therefore, did not repeal the common law within a factual situation where an in loco parentis was guilty of using immoderate force while exercising domestic authority over a child. Further, the placement of the statutory crime on the felony plateau signified the elevation of guilt and punishment. When the legislative intent was to deal more harshly with aggravated forms of already criminal behavior, there was no inherent incompatibility between the greater and lesser crimes and there was no preempting and no repeal of the lesser, common law crime. Also, there were so many potential utilities to the common law crime that the court could not conceive of any remote legislative purpose or intent to repeal it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment with costs to be paid by defendant.

 

1183 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Supervisor of Assessments v. St. Leonard Shores Joint Venture


No. 260, September Term, 1984


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


61 Md. App. 204; 486 A.2d 206; 1985 Md. App. LEXIS 283



January 8, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CALVERT COUNTY, PERRY G. BOWEN, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CALVERT COUNTY FOR THE PURPOSE OF ENTERING A JUDGMENT CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Supervisor of Assessments of Calvert County, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Calvert County (Maryland), which reversed the decision of the Maryland Tax Court affirming the assessment by the supervisor against property owned by appellee landowner.


OVERVIEW: The landowner owned a large tract of property which was subdivided into various lots. The Supervisor did not consider the bulk ownership in accordance with Md. Dep't Assessment & Taxation Directive (November 13, 1980). The landowner contended that in order to have assessed the property's value properly, the assessor must have considered the estimated period of time required to sell the lots. The court held that (1) the State Department of Assessments and Taxation was clearly empowered to promulgate a directive instructing assessors as to what factors to consider; (2) the method of assessment utilized by the assessor was a factual determination within his administrative expertise; (3) the substantive contents and application of the directive was subject to review under the "rational basis test" and should have been upheld as it was supported by the facts and had a reasonable basis in law; (4) there was no per se method of assessment which must be followed; and (5) application of the directive resulted in fair, uniform assessments.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the circuit court for the purpose of entering a judgment consistent with the court's opinion. Costs were to be paid by the landowner.

 

1184 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. State


No. 385, September Term, 1984


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


61 Md. App. 94; 484 A.2d 1050; 1984 Md. App. LEXIS 462



December 12, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY, NEAL JANEY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL OF BALTIMORE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged her conviction by the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) for criminal contempt. Defendant was convicted after she failed to appear for trial in a separate charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was served with a written summons to appear in a criminal trial in the trial court. When the date and time of her trial arrived, she did not appear. A bench warrant for her apprehension was issued. Later that day, defendant appeared in the courtroom. When apprised that defendant was present, the judge called upon her to answer for the failure to appear. Defendant told the judge that she had gone to the wrong courthouse and that only after that court finished its assignment for the day did she realize that she was in the wrong place. The trial court found defendant guilty of contempt for failure to appear and sentenced her to an 89-day jail term. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that it was unable to conclude that defendant's non-appearance in the trial court when her case was called was either an open insult to the court or the judge or a resistance to the powers of the judge. Defendant's belated appearance caused some inconvenience to the judge, the witnesses, and the prosecution, but it did not interrupt the business of the court. The court found that the trial court was not justified in adjudging defendant to be in direct criminal contempt under Md. R. 1a.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for criminal contempt.

 

1185 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Howell v. State


No. 150, September Term, 1984


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


60 Md. App. 463; 483 A.2d 780; 1984 Md. App. LEXIS 431



November 14, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY JAMES H. TAYLOR, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which convicted defendant of grand theft after his pretrial motion to suppress evidence was denied.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of grand theft based upon an agreed statement of facts. Defendant contended on appeal that the trial court erroneously denied his pretrial motion to suppress the fruits of an executed search and seizure warrant. The court affirmed the judgment against defendant. The court determined that the Fourth Amendment exclusionary rule did not apply to the failure of an applicant to sign an application for the warrant in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 551 (Supp. 1984). The court further determined that the heavy social price of excluding probative evidence under the Fourth Amendment was not appropriate because an officer had acted in good faith reliance on a judicially issued search and seizure warrant. The court found that Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 26 had not been violated because there was no violation of the Fourth Amendment. The court concluded that the sanction of exclusion was not available for a violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 551 (Supp. 1984).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of grand theft.

Curry v. State


No. 1736, September Term, 1983


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


60 Md. App. 171; 481 A.2d 812; 1984 Md. App. LEXIS 419



October 4, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied January 8, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY ELSBETH LEVY BOTHE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of judgments of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which convicted them, upon retrial, of kidnapping and sentenced them to 30 years of imprisonment under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 337 (1982).


OVERVIEW: Defendants were initially convicted of first degree murder, kidnapping, and use of a handgun in the commission of a felony. The trial court erred in denying their motions for mistrial based on prosecutorial misconduct, and the original convictions were reversed. Upon retrial, the trial court convicted them of kidnapping and sentenced them to 30 years of imprisonment under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 337 (1982). Defendants sought review and contended that the trial court erred in denying their motion to dismiss on the ground of double jeopardy. The court held that, without specific prosecutorial intent, neither prosecutorial overreaching nor harassment would bar a retrial, and it further found that double jeopardy barred a retrial only when a prosecutor attempted to "sabotage" a trial. Because there was no evidence of such overreaching sabotage conduct by the prosecutor, the court held that the trial court had not abused its discretion in denying defendants' second motion for a retrial. Further, the court determined that the trial judge was permitted to impose a sentence within the guidelines of § 337. The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments.

 

1187 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


State v. One Hundred & Fifty-Eight Gaming Devices


No. 934, September Term, 1983


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


59 Md. App. 44; 474 A.2d 545; 1984 Md. App. LEXIS 358



May 8, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] TWO APPEALS FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY JAMES L. WRAY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART AND VACATED IN PART; CASE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDING CONSISTENT HEREWITH. COSTS TO BE DIVIDED EQUALLY BETWEEN ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY AND APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appeal arose from a petition for the forfeiture of gaming devices seized from defendant corporation. The corporation's motion for summary judgment was denied. The State's petition was granted by the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) with respect to those gaming devices found to be slot machines and with respect to a sum of money taken from the corporation's office. The State appealed and the corporation cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court found that there was no statutory authority for the State to seize the 158 purported gaming devices from the corporation. The State did, however, have the common law right to require forfeiture of contraband. It held that slot machines were contraband, and thus the State had the right to such forfeiture. The trial court correctly decided that the statutory exception allowed to possessors of antique slot machines was applicable to the corporation, notwithstanding that the machines were seized six months before the statute became effective. The court held that one looks to the date the forfeiture action was begun, rather than the date of seizure. The trial court impermissibly delegated to the State the task of determining which of the seized non-fungible machines, other than those introduced into evidence, violated Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 264B. It was for the court to make the determination. The cash seized by the police was not contraband, because it was not seized or captured by any police officer in connection with any arrest for the playing or operation of any gaming devices.


OUTCOME: The matter was remand to the trial court for a specific finding as to which machines were forfeitable and which were not. The State was instructed to show, by a preponderance of the evidence, that each of the devices seized violated the statute. The forfeiture of the cash was error; thus, the court reversed that portion of the order and direct that the money be returned.

 

1188 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Cohen v. Goldstein


No. 561, September Term, 1983


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


58 Md. App. 699; 474 A.2d 229; 1984 Md. App. LEXIS 362



May 4, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTOMERY COUNTY WILLIAM W. WENNER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant magistrate appealed from an adverse judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) in his action seeking a declaratory judgment that he was entitled to the 14 years, two months of credit claimed by him in the retirement system. Appellees were the appropriate officials of the judicial pension plan.


OVERVIEW: The magistrate was about five months shy of 10 years of creditable service in the judicial pension plan upon reaching his 70 birthday, and sought to earn credit for continued employment as a master after his 70th birthday so that he was entitled by virtue of Md. Ann. Code art. 65, § 88, to an additional three years and eight months by reason of active military service during World War II. The court found that he was not able to do so. It found that masters who were members of State Employees' Retirement System (SERS) did not have the status of appointed officials, and were therefore subject to the mandatory retirement provision of Md. Ann. Code art. 73B, § 11(1)(b). They were legally ineligible for the military credit unless they attained 10 years of creditable service in the retirement system prior to their 70th birthday. The court found that whatever their actual ability to continue serving after reaching the age of 70, for purposes of SERS they were regarded as retired as of the first day of the month following their 70th birthday.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1189 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Sproates v. State


No. 975, September Term, 1983


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


58 Md. App. 547; 473 A.2d 1289; 1984 Md. App. LEXIS 333



April 13, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR KENT COUNTY GEORGE B. RASIN, JR. JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment by the Circuit Court for Kent County (Maryland) convicting him of possession of and intent to distribute marijuana, possession of drug paraphernalia, and a handgun violation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in failing to suppress the evidence obtained from a warrantless search. The court disagreed. The trial court correctly denied defendant's suppression motion because the officer's activities occurred in an uninhabited open area. Even though the trooper had committed a technical trespass, under the circumstances he had a right to make the investigation and attempt to verify the information that was furnished him by an informant. The trailers where the marijuana was found were in an open field and beyond the pale of the Fourth Amendment, and thus the search was lawful. The trailer was located beyond the curtilage of defendant's house. There was no indication that the trailer or the surrounding area was used for habitation. There was no exhibition of a subjective expectation of privacy. No signs or fences precluded entry onto the land. Likewise, defendant displayed no subjective expectation of privacy over the contents of the trailer. There was no door or lock. There was no sign demonstrating ownership or warning trespassers to go away. The drying marijuana was clearly visible from outside the trailer.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1190 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Elliott v. Kupferman


No. 935, September Term, 1983


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


58 Md. App. 510; 473 A.2d 960; 1984 Md. App. LEXIS 331



April 12, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HARFORD COUNTY BRODNAX CAMERON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANTS TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, former police chief (police chief) and his wife, sought review of the order of the Circuit Court for Harford County (Maryland), which granted appellee town commissioners' (commissioners) demurrer on a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim and dismissed the remaining tort claims based on governmental immunity pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 23A, § 1B(a).


OVERVIEW: After the commissioners fired the police chief, then initiated a disciplinary action against him after he was reinstated, and then failed to reinstate him after his term expired, the police chief and his wife filed an action against the commissioners. The trial court granted a demurrer on the 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim and dismissed the tort claims. The court affirmed the judgment on appeal, holding that (1) the police chief did not have a § 1983 claim stemming from a property interest in continued employment because there was no statutory or contractual entitlement, nor did the Law-Enforcement Officers' Bill of Rights, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, §§ 727-734D, confer a property right; rather, it merely afforded procedural safeguards during investigations and hearings, (2) even if he had a property interest, the police chief failed to allege a deprivation of his interest without due process of law, (3) the commissioners' actions were immune from the tort claims because their conduct was a discretionary function and because the police chief and his wife failed to allege malice in some claims and presented only conclusory allegations of malice in the other claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which granted the commissioners' demurrer on the police chief's § 1983 claim, and which dismissed the tort claims based on governmental immunity. The court held that the police chief did not have a property interest in continued employment to support the § 1983 claim, and he did not allege facts to support malice and overcome the governmental immunity defense.

Metropolitan Life Ins. Co. v. Insurance Commissioner of Maryland


No. 881, September Term, 1983


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


58 Md. App. 457; 473 A.2d 933; 1984 Md. App. LEXIS 321



April 11, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY JOSEPH I. PINES, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance company appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which was in favor of appellee, the state insurance commissioner, over the amount of premium tax due by the insurance company.


OVERVIEW: The dispute arose from a difference of opinion concerning the application of Maryland's "retaliatory" premium tax pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 48A, § 61(1), which required an out of state insurance company to be taxed at the same rate as a hypothetical Maryland company doing the same amount of business in that state. The issue was how to properly calculate the "retaliatory" premium due to the additional premium tax New York City imposed on policies insuring risks located in the city separate from the New York State tax. The insurance company contended that the last sentence of § 61(1) was unconstitutional because of vagueness and because it improperly delegated legislative authority to the commissioner to determine how to calculate that tax. The legislature told the insurance commissioner to regard local taxes as though they were imposed by the State, and left it to him to determine the most appropriate method of doing so. The court found that this was not an impermissible delegation of the power to make law, but rather the authority to implement and enforce the expressed legislative will.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1192 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Coleman v. Coleman


No. 1643, September Term, 1983


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


57 Md. App. 755; 471 A.2d 1115; 1984 Md. App. LEXIS 290



March 5, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Montgomery County Stanley B. Frosh, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which denied his request for an injunction preventing appellee wife from having a fetus aborted.


OVERVIEW: The husband filed a petition to prevent the wife from having a fetus aborted. The pregnancy was terminated, but the court decided to address the merits because the subject was one that was likely to arise again and again. The court affirmed the trial court's decision denying the husband's petition for injunctive relief. Md. Code Ann., Health-Gen. § 20-208 was unconstitutional insofar as it conflicted with decisions of the United States Supreme Court. A state's interest in regulating abortion was not compelling until approximately the end of the first trimester of pregnancy. Until that time, a woman was permitted to decide, without state interference, whether to have an abortion. The husband did not have a Ninth Amendment right to defend his preborn child because preborn children did not have rights under the federal common law. The husband did not have standing to enjoin his wife from having an abortion because a husband's consent to a wife's abortion, during the first trimester, was unnecessary. The wife was entitled to a medically induced abortion during the first trimester, notwithstanding the objections of the state or any other person, firm, corporation, or association.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision denying the husband's petition to prevent his wife from having a fetus aborted.

Macon v. State


No. 226, September Term, 1983


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


57 Md. App. 705; 471 A.2d 1090; 1984 Md. App. LEXIS 284



March 2, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE Circuit Court for Prince George's County Robert J. Woods, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which convicted him of knowingly distributing obscene material in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 418.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of knowingly distributing obscene material in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 418. Defendant sought review and contended that, because there had been no prior judicial determination of obscenity and because no warrant had been issued authorizing the police to seize the alleged obscene material, the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress. Although obscenity was not within the area of constitutionally protected speech or press, the court found that the line between speech unconditionally guaranteed and speech which could have been regulated was finely drawn. The court held that the need to protect First Amendment rights from government suppression necessitated more stringent application of Fourth Amendment safeguards in obscenity cases than in other criminal cases. The court determined that a judicial officer was to determine whether material was obscene prior to granting the police a warrant to seize such material. Because the police failed to obtain judgment as to whether defendant's material was obscene, they lacked the requisite probable cause to seize the material. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and found that the police lacked probable cause to seize the material because they failed to obtain judicial determination as to whether defendant's material was obscene.

In re Dan D.


No. 534, September Term, 1983


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


57 Md. App. 522; 470 A.2d 1318; 1984 Md. App. LEXIS 273



February 8, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF MONTGOMERY COUNTY DOUGLAS H. MOORE, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS REVERSED; MONTGOMERY COUNTY TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the father of a delinquent minor, sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Montgomery County (Maryland), which imposed an order of restitution on the father, mother, and the delinquent minor, for the acts of the minor.


OVERVIEW: The minor was adjudged delinquent in three cases based on charges of daytime housebreaking. The State filed petitions for restitution against the minor and both his parents. The trial court entered restitution orders and the father appealed. The father's appeal challenged the constitutionality of Md. Code Ann. Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-829 and argued that it did not apply to the father as a non-custodial parent. The court did not consider those arguments but did reverse the restitution orders on the ground that no evidence was presented at the restitution hearing to prove that the minor committed the acts. Such evidence had been presented in the adjudicatory proceeding, and the minor was found delinquent. However, the restitution proceeding was separate, and no attempt was made to either repeat the evidence or to incorporate the record of the prior proceeding. The only evidence presented in the restitution proceeding concerned the property that was damaged, but there was nothing in the record to indicate that the minor was responsible for the damage.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgments imposing restitution.

Elprin v. Howard County Bd. of Education


No. 428, September Term, 1983


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


57 Md. App. 458; 470 A.2d 833; 1984 Md. App. LEXIS 262



February 6, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied June 7, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal From The CIRCUIT COURT FOR HOWARD COUNTY J. THOMAS NISSEL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens requested review by the Maryland State Board of Education of a decision by appellee, a county board of education, to close two elementary schools. The Board upheld the county board's decision. The Circuit Court for Howard County (Maryland) granted the county board's motion to dismiss the citizens' appeal for lack of subject matter jurisdiction on the ground that it did not involve a "contested case." The citizens appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the citizens' appeal on the ground that it did not involve a "contested case." On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that decisions made by the Board in matters of school consolidation and closure were quasi-legislative in nature and were not appealable under the Administrative Procedure Act as "contested cases." The court found that the county board had discretionary power pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Educ., §§ 4-108(c), 4-114(c), and 4-119(a) to determine the geographic attendance of schools and to consolidate and close schools when practicable. The court determined that such actions by the county board were policy making or quasi-legislative proceedings. The court concluded that the case did not involve the citizens' "legal rights" because there was no right or privilege to attend a particular school under state law. The court found that the Board's decision to accept the citizens' appeal did not render the case "contested." The court determined that the citizens were not guaranteed judicial review because the Board was not obligated to hear an appeal that did not involve a decision by a school superintendent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which dismissed the citizens' appeal.

Berlin v. Aluisi


No. 1230, September Term, 1983


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


57 Md. App. 390; 470 A.2d 388; 1984 Md. App. LEXIS 261



February 2, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal From The CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY ROBERT H. MASON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlord sought review of the order of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which denied the landlord's prayers for writ of mandamus, injunction, declaratory judgment, damages, and action on the sheriff's bond, in the landlord's action against appellees, sheriff, his deputy, the bonding company, and landlord's tenant, for the sheriff's failure to evict the tenant despite the tenant's tender of the rent due.


OVERVIEW: The landlord filed a summary ejectment complaint for the tenant's failure to pay rent. Judgment was entered for the landlord for the amount of rent owed and for restitution of the premises. A warrant of restitution was issued. A deputy sheriff arrived at the tenant's home to execute the warrant of restitution by evicting the tenant. The tenant then tendered to the landlord the amount due according to the warrant. The landlord demanded that the tenant pay all of the rent then due, including the current month. When the tenant refused to pay the additional amount, the landlord requested that the deputy carry out the eviction. In accordance with the sheriff's standard procedures, the deputy refused to carry out the eviction and allowed the tenant to remain on the premises. The court affirmed the lower court's order denying the landlord's petition for writ of mandamus, injunction, declaratory judgment, damages, and action on the sheriff's bond against the sheriff. The court held that the trial court's interpretation that the amount that may be tendered by a tenant to redeem the premises after a judgment for restitution was the rent and fees judicially ordered to be due was correct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order, finding that the trial court's interpretation of the statute that all past due rent and late fees payable by a tenant in order to redeem the premises after a judgment for restitution has been entered meant rent and fees that have been judicially declared to be due was correct.

Maryland-National Capital Park & Planning Com. v. Friendship Heights


No. 182, September Term, 1983


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


57 Md. App. 69; 468 A.2d 1353; 1984 Md. App. LEXIS 240



January 6, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied June 7, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: TWO APPEALS FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY Philip M. Fairbanks, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED. REMANDED FOR ENTRY OF AN ORDER AFFIRMING THE DECISION OF THE MARYLAND NATIONAL CAPITAL PARK AND PLANNING COMMISSION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY FRIENDSHIP HEIGHTS, MARYLAND NATIONAL CAPITAL PARK AND PLANNING COMMISSION AND COMMUNITY SOMERSET ASSOCIATES IN EQUAL SHARES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant planning commission and appellees, residents' development (residents) and applicant for a development plan (applicant), sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) in an action for an application for approval of a site plan.


OVERVIEW: The commission approved the applicant's site plan (plan). The residents appealed to the trial court, which dismissed the appeal on the grounds that the approval of the plan was not a contested matter under the Administrative Procedure Act (APA). However, the trial court ruled for the residents in the event that its jurisdictional determination was wrong. All parties appealed. The court ruled for the commission. The court held that the residents had standing to challenge the plan, though its property was not in the plan, because the plan involved a ring road, which directly affected their interests. The commission had standing to appeal the decision that the approval was not a contested matter under the APA because the commission's decision could have been challenged years later. Because of the nature of the commission's rules and that the approval process was a quasi-judicial decision because of factual determinations, the approval was a contested matter and, therefore, the trial court had jurisdiction to review the commission's decision. There was substantial evidence under Montgomery County, Md., Code ch. 59, § 59-D-3 (1977) to support the commission's decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision, ruled for the commission and for the applicant, and ruled against the residents in the action for approval of a site plan.

 

1198 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Mayfield v. State


No. 99, September Term, 1983


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


56 Md. App. 541; 468 A.2d 400; 1983 Md. App. LEXIS 406



December 12, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY (formerly the Criminal Court of Baltimore) ROBERT I. H. HAMMERMAN, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; REMANDED FOR NEW TRIAL; COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL OF BALTIMORE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which convicted defendant of two counts of robbery with a deadly weapon and two related counts of use of a handgun in the commission of a crime of violence. The trial court did not allow defendant to testify in his own behalf although he rescinded his waiver of his right to testify after the trial court ruled that defendant's mother could not testify.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the robbery was a drug deal gone awry and a prelude to an extortion scheme. After defendant elected not to testify, defense counsel offered the testimony of defendant's mother to establish that the accusers offered not to testify in exchange for money. The trial court sustained the state's objection to the mother's testimony because she had not been sequestered during the state's case-in-chief. When the trial resumed the next day, defendant told the court he wanted to testify because his mother's testimony had been disallowed. The trial court did not permit defendant to testify and convicted defendant as charged. On appeal, the court reversed because the trial court abused its discretion by not permitting defendant to testify. The court held that defendant had a statutory, and perhaps a constitutional, right to testify in his own behalf. Defendant waived his right without knowing that his mother could not testify and rescinded the waiver after the trial court's ruling. The state did not proffer that it would have difficulty in securing the rebuttal testimony of the local witnesses nor that it would be prejudiced by permitting defendant to reopen his case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions and remanded for a new trial because the trial court abused its discretion by not permitting defendant to reopen his case.

 

1199 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Burroughs v. Raynor


No. 1247, September Term, 1983


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


56 Md. App. 432; 468 A.2d 141; 1983 Md. App. LEXIS 398



December 7, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal From The CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY. THOMAS WARD, JUDGE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, applicants for city council membership, filed a petition for mandamus asking the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) to direct appellee city board of supervisors of elections to place their names on the ballot as independent candidates. The trial court denied the petition. The applicants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The applicants to sought election to the city council. To obtain a place on the November ballot, each filed with the administrator of the city board of supervisors of elections a signed nominating petition. The board deducted from the petitions the signatures of those who were not listed as voters registered in the applicants' district. At the conclusion of that process, the board determined that the petitions fell short of the required names and refused to certify the applicants as candidates. The applicants filed a petition for mandamus asking the circuit court to direct the board to place their names on the ballot. The circuit court denied the petition. On appeal, the court affirmed that judgment. The court held that, pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 33, § 7-1, the board had the authority to review the petitions and to keep their names off the ballot because the petitions were not signed by a sufficient numbers of registered voters. The court also held that the legislature's delegation of that authority to the board was not an unconstitutional usurpation of judicial powers because the board's action was subject to judicial review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the applicants' petition.

 

1200 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Commission on Medical Discipline v. McDonnell


No. 1921, September Term, 1982


Court of Special Appeals of Maryland


56 Md. App. 391; 467 A.2d 1072; 1983 Md. App. LEXIS 391



November 14, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Granted April 5, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal From The CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY (formerly the Baltimore City Court) J. HAROLD GRADY, Judge



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED PURSUANT TO MD.RULE 1071. CASE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Commission on Medical Discipline (commission), sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) reversing the commission's decision that found appellee physician guilty of a violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 43, § 130(h)(8), immoral conduct of a physician in his practice as a physician, and issued a reprimand. The issue concerned the physician's conduct in a separate medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: In a disciplinary proceeding, the commission found that the physician's conduct in a preceding malpractice action in tampering with expert witnesses was in violation of art. 43, § 130(h)(8). The trial court reversed the commission's decision. The trial court found that the commission reached erroneous legal conclusions in finding that the physician's conduct was immoral within the meaning of art. 43, § 130(h)(8) and that such conduct occurred in his practice as a physician. On further review, the court vacated the judgment and remanded the cause for further proceedings. The court found that the commission, with its expertise, could have found that even the seemingly innocuous message that transcripts of their testimony would have been forwarded to appropriate medical societies, delivered to the recipients' mentors, would have naturally tended to intimidate the expert witnesses and constrict their testimony. The physician's conduct amounted to an endeavor to obstruct justice. The commission could have legally concluded that a physician's attempt to protect and preserve his professional reputation was conduct in his practice as a physician.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment from the trial court that had reversed a decision from the commission finding that the physician had tampered with the expert witnesses in a preceding malpractice action against the physician. The court remanded the cause for further proceedings.
